Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	In the work of this chapter, there are often bleedings when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in treating wounds, and extracting arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come for healing.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from such people who are so with their disease that they die immediately because of the harm they find in their disease, and the greatness of its malice; and of these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are those who give you their senses, and say: "Wait, I am in pain"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not necessary to grant permission to those who come to you with this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your desire, and do not open foolishly but wisely of that which you are certain and have taken and lost; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your illnesses for the sake of converting health; and this will help you to gain good reputation, glory, and memory for a long time.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Lords give you good understanding and truth, and if you wish to breathe from the holy inspiration of his hand, indeed.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered you to study this chapter by comparing it with other chapters on cauteries, as I advised from the beginning to the end, because you will find it easier to understand what you will have to do.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full of sharp
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often occurs in children when they are being born, and when the baby's head is held too tightly; and sometimes it comes from a reason that one does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	I have never seen this disease except in children, and all those that I have seen died; and therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in the hands of others.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	I saw a child who was suffering from a sharp pain, and the head was swelling each day until it could no longer be borne; and he thought so much of the moisture that he died, and this moisture is gathered outside the bone above the sphenoid, between the skull and the bone; and the works are such if the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, then make a wide incision on the head; and let it be as long as our finger, so that the moisture flows; and remove the shape of the spatula.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more extensive, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, like this:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the commissures of the neck open on each part, and the sharp pain when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not return: then you must make three cuts in the neck in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After closing the cuts with bandages and powders, and applying wine and oil, let it rest for five days; then remove it, and treat the wound with tents and counter-irritants, and keep the neck still, and gradually introduce dry meat without moisture until the member is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at the size of the abscess and the angle of the sharp instrument; for it is never in front, never behind, never on the right, and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore cut the abscess where it is open, and fill it with the sharp instrument, and make the incision according to what you can do; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and if blood flows, the hairs may die from the flow of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of return
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to someone who has a disease called "cataract" in their eyes or at the base, and the disease is ancient, and the medical treatment does not help much, then the remedy is cauterization with what covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, while you look at it, to make the hairs on their head stand; then rub the neck with a rough cloth until the arteries open, then hold the hairs against the cloth; then look where the vein is, and the two are near the ears, and they are not replaced; then sign the two with ink, then cover one and the other with a piece of cloth of two parts, until the wound comes just to the bone, and it should be through the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, push the piece of cloth away from the artery and cover it above, cutting as it should through the middle.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if blood spurts out continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at the first prick, it is necessary to measure the amount of space between three fingers, then bend and cut into the bone; and the amount of sinew that needs to be removed is six centimeters, and possibly a little more or less depending on what the wound can bear, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone point sharp, if the coping that we have applied does not come out, then cover the wound and bind, and the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of the head
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old headache comes, and the catarrh is strong, due to the moisture of tears and the heat in the temples and old age and similar things, and it is treated by methods of medical cures and nothing seems to help, then we should cauterize the arteries of the temples and burn, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of their extraction is that the hairs of his temples face backwards, and listen to the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and it is not restored until in some men who are too fat; and if it is restored, then strain the skin with some cloths, then rub the leather with any rough cloth, and raise the leather with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the sponge of which this is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then cut it upwards with pincers, and pull out many threads that are stuck to each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it to the tip of the needle, then cover that part according to the amount of the two injuries.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if it is not covered, it will not heal completely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from the sixth century, just to the third; and if the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it in two places with a strong silk thread that does not allow any blood to come before the scab of the wound, and does not allow any discharge of blood; then cover the excess between the two threads in the same hour, and then, if you see, if the fire cautery is applied just to the bone until the injuries are covered; and this is the best work, if the pains are not feverish and he is of a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery, it is used to finish off the moistures: because it is of greater help against moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	When it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one should fill the wound with old cotton and place dry bandages on top; and when they are removed, one should treat with dry medicines that cause heat to rise, and bandages, until they are healed; and if without cutting the artery as much as you can work, then quickly cover it with a cauterizer, or fill the wound with vinegar and apply it to your hand that the uncut part is not frozen; and if you do not have this present, then place ice on the wound for as long as the uncut part is not frozen, and rise the wound with cold water until it is healed, and it should be kept dry. What is more difficult and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cauterizer cutting from II parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to last longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When instruments are too tight, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be between the two knives a space of large width, and then when you have marked the two lines, and you melt the iron hot until it comes close to the bone, and cover the vein in two lines; and they should be separated between the two lines because it is not safe from this cauterization at all; and this is the form of the cauterization:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are above the surface of the head, and it does not improve with medical treatment, and you see the face of the pain twisted, and feels like a tremor; and they are held and moist so that the hair of the papers is soaked, and the papers are crumpled, and burned by the heat of the tears, if it is necessary for this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the ancient "wound healer," and you should make three cuts evenly along the length of the wound; one of the cuts should be as two teeth below the front, and the others two along the ribs above the bones, and guard against cutting the arteries that are along the ribs above the bones; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and each wound the quantity of three doses across the wound; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth to soak up the blood, then plug the wound with the shape of two parts of which this is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made from the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the skin that is between the two cuts down to the face which is above the bone, then make another cut from the other side of the same incision to the second, and then extract this piece.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument called "cultellaire" in the first cut, it is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side of the instrument towards the edge of the skin and the blunt side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the other cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And apply compresses to all the vessels that descend from the head as far as the eyes until the incision is complete up to where the wound opens, and then make another one in the same place on the other side; and then extract the arrow equally, and express the blood for the arrow taken; then put in each incision a piece of old cotton, and put on dressings made of meal and wine and oil and vinegar, and ensure that abscesses do not come; and the next day remove the bandage, and apply a great deal of ground ivy, then the cure of basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures as one cures wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	The return of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Regarding any person who comes for cauterization as usual, and you see the eyes closed and small, and weakened vision, and the papers burned; and the hairs are shaved, and where the shaving is done, there is pain, and the hairs are clogged; consequently, these accidents and that cauterization come from many wounds, and the healing that is, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is whether you command the patient to turn his head back, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another wide in the temple.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it begins from the temple on the right side to the temple on the left, and let the incision be just to the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at the sides; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood onto a sponge, and then drain between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton, and linen; then bandage with moistened cloths in wine and oil, and guard against abscess forming; when it is taken out, it is necessary to rub the bone until charcoal begins to form, then care for things that cause excision, which are used to smear char.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of clay, and make a poultice; and administer it in these wounds to apply honey for all.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which sticks in the ears is one of the four things: grains, or beasts, or stone of the mine or similar things like iron; or seeds, such as lentils, beans, and peas; or things that flow, such as water and milk and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it sticks in the ear stone or other kind of thing that does not stick to the ear, does not grow in the ear, put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the arrow, if any amount of purple oil or hemlock oil is poured on it, then proceed with extraction; and this causes the patient to vomit from discomfort, and when they vomit, cover their nostrils, and put pieces of cloth or wool around their ear; and hold the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times vomiting occurs from this treatment; and if it does not occur, then proceed with extraction using fine forceps, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it vomits with the forceps, it is good; if not, then proceed with extraction using fine needles of small double thread; and if it does not vomit with these, then make a thin layer of beeswax and put it over the ear or in the opening of the ear canal very thickly so that nothing can enter with the needle; then remove it carefully, for many times vomiting occurs as we have said; and if it does not vomit in this way, then take some gauze and wrap it around the ear, and put any instrument that is sharp at the point to make, and put a little cotton inside; then press the gauze on the arrow or whatever else, and remove it carefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not jump from all these things that we have said, then quickly cut through the ear as soon as abscess and blood come out, and spasm; and the manner of the cut is that you first make a small incision in the painful part of the cephalic, and extract the pus according to its virtue, then place the pus between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat or flesh depends; and the cut should be like a moon, as far as you come to the bone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it vigorously at your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is small and inflamed, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer the following remedy in a subtle form according to this formula:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make this mistake when you think the grains are moist due to earwax, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine tweezers and the succier, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of a grain that gets stuck in the ear, it is necessary to use a stream of warm water and clean the ear thoroughly with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it lie across the ear itself or where the sharp is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out because of the sky, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many needles according to the length of your thumb and light ones, and heat them in the fire; and put the hairs of one ear underneath another, and strike with another needle from the other side of the foot, and strike with another needle from above the ear; and do not stop doing this needle after needle until the sharp is completely out, and so it will all come out; and if you see, take the wire, and burn one of the hairs in the ear, and the other hair take with fire until the thinnest wire is melted; then make another wire as we have said in the needle.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is of small size, as with a mouse and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that one can feel, then alleviate extraction with pincers; and it is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms in the ears, if you cure them as we have said in the division and treat distillations, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary to look into the ear with sunlight: if there are no worms, then remove them with fine pincers, and if there are none, then take the cotton of this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And apply the most subtle pressure on the ear according to the amount of pain, then it is often successful for the entire head; do this frequently until all the vertebrae are visible.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not comply, dull the pain around the head with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they still do not succeed, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in the treatment of vertebrae, and you will find them where you can treat distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether of silver or lead is placed below the small pores, and above the covers to distill; and to press within the distillation with a well-made silver instrument for this purpose, and if you see take the razor and wrap it around the point evenly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you see from your medicines in the cane, and the cane should be in the ear; then press inside the razor all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or slightly out of the ear; and the smell is inside, and the distillations are the little pot heated at the fire just as it is distilled in the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be very good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stupor of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some sort of hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by stupor of wound, or of charred flesh within the ear, and this stupor never comes from inside the ear, unless one cannot see it; and it always comes from outside the ear, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes from inside the ear, if one cannot see it, is due to great pain in many positions, and in this case where one sees it, one should put the ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the opacification apparent, if the work has all this space of because of which this form is:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And so, behind and in front of the ear, so that it does not burst the ear; if the swelling is from the ear or the bone of the ear, then hold it with fine forceps, and the scalpel lightly, until that char is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the swelling is inside the ear, then take a fine scalpel lightly and burn it slightly over the fire, then put it where the bone of the ear is.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the swelling that the patient feels is gritty to hear, lightly pierce, and make sure you do not damage the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten with Egyptian mummification.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not apply any bandage until the wound is clean, or take a tent and moisten it with strong rose water, and powder it with vitriol broken into small pieces; and if you see swelling in the ear, then it is advisable to remove the tent and apply another tent made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it as soon as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is bleeding from the wound, soak a sponge and apply cold cloths, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding of blood which are used to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the char of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method for removing thorns that come from papers when they are wet and dry, if it is necessary to extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the tip of a glass from their roots; then place on the wound vitreous powder.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without decortication, the patient is cauterized with a fine lens-shaped cauterizer, and the cauterizer after the incision is suitable; and often they recur, nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	For the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times in papers come things that seem like gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this disease is called "hail," and it is an assembly of moisture large on the paper above and below; the work is such: if the hail moves from one part to another, and it is a light thing to know; then make it wide, then scrape each part lightly, then take it with pincers, and cover it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not cover it with a thin layer of paper, it does not hurt the patient; and if the pressure is great, it assembles at one seam, and the cure until it is healthy; and if it is small, do not force it, because the pains will restore soon and injure.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the splinter is falling downwards into the inner part of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and put the splinter into some tweezers, and hold it with a cloth on both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it does not hurt anything; and when the splinter is removed, pour in some vinegar oil until the wound is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is smeared on papers above, and it has more in children than in adults, and it hurts their eyes, and they vomit it in the morning, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears stick to their eyes; and because they lie on their faces, they sleep on their backs, and their papers are outside their eyelids moist with exinach that has dissolved into oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb to your touch and feel the excruciation between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the work is such that the painful part is placed on your hand; then take a cloth of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains excruciation from each part, then place it over it; and press on one side and the other, so that the excruciation is assembled within the circle; then, with a sharp spatula, cut a slit of a certain width, and not larger than the wound on the vein; and cut the skin until you come to the excruciation; and in many positions, excruciation comes from the slit, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the bandage from all around the piece of cloth between your two hands, and turn your hand to the right and left as much as possible; and be careful not to insert it into the wound, that you do not come to the whole length of the oil, that you do not hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not insert at the beginning of the wound, slightly push the wound as we have said; then extract it as we have said, then wipe off cloths in oil and vinegar, and put on the limb, and bind it tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who bite and put on to corrupt the moisture that is remaining.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as they are healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the limb with an abscess, then the healer should apply ointments until they are healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs are born not according to nature, and are awake, they harm the eyes, and bring on various diseases such as tears and softening of the papers and corneal, until it is the cause of destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cauterization with fire, or by medicine cold according to what is before or in the chapter of cauterization, and is done either by incision and stitching or by cauterizing, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the painful part in your hand, then return the paper of oil to your right hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is an needle at the end of all the thread; and so it is above the margin of the paper or where the hair grows among these hairs, and pull the thread above the paper, and return it to the razor; then in the part outside the paper, outside the hairs adjusted, all the skin from the big toe to the small one; then pull the thread, and place outside the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then above the paper a figure of a bandage, like the foot of a mullet, and in all cases it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you saw lift the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If you have skill in handling great quantities of paper according to how the paper is softened; then make all the spatula above the two lines that you have signed, and begin from the greatest arm down to the smallest; and let one of the wounds be near the natural hairs at the base of the root, then cut the thread in one of the two angles of the needle, then scrape the skin; then bring together the two lips to a seam of an needle all along the thread of fine silk, and suck the blood, and dry the superfluity of the threads above the two sides of any things gluing, if you see that you make it; and if not, if you do not have care for it, then leave the seam and the threads near three or four days; then cure the wound without seams of things dried and constricted, because the paper revives at the moment of the wound and its assemblement, but the seam is dry (as they say of the ancients), and it is work without fear; and if in another way: and that you sign the paper of a figure which is as equal to the shape of the mirror, as we have said, at three threads according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply this remedy with small equal forces according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or if it has a thread, put the thread in the shape; and the other thread over the big arm, and the second thread over the small one, and assemble the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin where you have marked, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with carron oil and similar soothing ointments; and never once has the hair of the skin been converted: if you use what we have said about the incision, but the sewing on one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The care of dogs is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and the needle inside according to what I have said, and then make two dogs by art, and two fine lines as long as the paper and the width of the space is; and cope with the two parts where you hold the threads; then bring together the one and the other subtly above what covers the paper of the oil, and strain the two dogs from the two parts form; and leave it in this way for some time, and the skin that was stretched will die and rot and putrefy, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it lingers, if the copper has some strength, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound has been dressed, and if it has been lifted off the paper, and they will not grow back the hair; and this is the form of the two cains that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a thin needle, and draw out the silk thread softly and thinly; then assemble the hairs and pull them gently, and let the lengths of the threads be one palm long; then order the other thin silk thread briefly, and pull the heads of the hairs together; then place the hairs on your skin so that the work is hidden, for it is a thin and delicate work, then draw the needle through the entire length of the hair rooted, and pierce it into the paper gently until you remove it from the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the top of the work, and pull in the work that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out entirely on the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the bone is treated and the hair does not come with it, then treat the bone with the oil until it comes out completely and you can see it through the vision of the oil; then take the bone and the oil, and close it and let it sit for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and heals; and if the hair is small, accompany it with one long hair from the goats naturally, and raise it with that one until it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the preparation of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the preparation of the oil, comes from the oil, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by wounding, or by cutting or by cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way of the work in it is that you break that suture, and dry the edges of it, and put in tents of linen, and tie it until it is healed; and it is only necessary to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will become worse than before; but in the work of things that are softening, such as fenugreek; and the rose of bitter or strong and seeds of linseed should be cooked, and wet with any of the oils, and it is wrapped in a tent, and the treatment of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your knowledge are that you should take care that it does not become misshapen like before; and this work that we have said is no more than an introduction to this disease, that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the oil that comes in the fat
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way of the work is that you grasp an needle, in which it has double thread, and the char in the fat, and make it pierce from the right arm to the left, so that the thread comes out at both ends; then the char is placed above all the needle, and the covering is wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what it should be, it is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the incision, and return the paper, and make two incisions where the cost of the paper is; and let the ones who have the two incisions at the angles of the incision that you have cut, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is as if it were a letter that has no «Greek»; then take that char, according to the quantity that its cost is away from, of what teaches the paper, then add the two missing parts, and tie them with a thread of linen; then care for what we have said about medicines that soften, and tents, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the illness comes from a cut or a stitch or a cauterization, it is necessary that you make a plain cut outside of the hairs and papers, as I have said; then squeeze between the two layers of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very different in form, and the wise masters compare all things possible to know how they can bring the figure back to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for work and tools in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this stitching is done by many people in a partly manner, where the paper above is glued with the white of the oil, and it cannot move or do its natural workings, then you must go outside the paper with the point of a razor, and lift it up; and stretch it with pincers, until you cut away what is hard to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too thin, so that the pain does not suffer from the spatula being too sharp or burning the oil; and let your incision, from which you scrape off this assembly, be lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and all this assembly is healed, and nothing is ever put into hot salted oil, and lifted out of cool sweet wine, and colloid; then place between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and put on top of the oil moillie wool in abundance of urine; and after the wound is healed use the colloid and other things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the elbow joint
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two types of elbow joints: one is nervous and resembles a hard, thick skin, and the other is not nervous but resembles frozen white moisture, which when touched with iron and heated with tongs and pincers, cannot be removed; and both start near the large arm and grow slowly until they cover the entire eye and light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of the incision is that the hairs put their head in your hand, then open the eyes; and lift the paper to your hand, then bend the elbow with pincers of small double, and put it above; then take a needle, and put the hair of a horse, or a goat, or a cow, and the thread strong; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the elbow, and push the thread through the entire needle, and tie the elbow with a thread and put it above, and scrape all the hair on the side of the elbow that shows the prunello and the silk to the hair just above, then cut the remaining at the root of the arm to all the subtle spatula and with small forces, and leave the natural skin of the arm, so that by the incision does not come the usual tears from the eyes; and once it has been extended only to the elbow, and the thread, as we have said; then scrape on all the soft spatula of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the intestines and break them, and that the scalpel is not perforated; and after the incision pour a little bit of broken silk thread oil, and a collar made of litharge, and leave it just above the other side; then care for what needs to be done until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the needle is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the needles cannot enter, often this resemblance of a needle of medicines; and they are born as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, then apply oil to the pain, and take the spatula lightly poured according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently rub the joint above, and if you see that it does not ease and the pain increases, then blow into a bowl of litharge colloid and red colloid and beaten silk, and dampen the oil with the other side; then continue the other work according to this same method, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, as if an abscess bursts, then milk it, and cure the abscess until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh on the arm is black due to great harm, then soak it in oil at night, and apply a part and not all at once, so that tears do not come; then pour in the oil a red powder made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men never have red flesh arise, and covers the pupil and restrains it above the papers and turns it to the side, and seems like a baluster rose; and if the work is that the hairs put their head in your safe, then work the ears, and cut all that flesh with suitable notches for this, and support it with force; then cover the first flesh, and go through scraping to the end, and make sure you do not bleed the oil at the work; and let the incision of the spanworm that we have said in the incision of the finger and as small forces of which one takes the base, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then use the oil of silk broiled or you distill red powder and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil afterwards with cotton with absinth, so that it is assured of no aposteme; and if nothing remains, and the swelling disappears, and you doubt aposteme, then leave the oil and cure the aposteme with calming remedies aposteme; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make many flesh is boiled in the oil by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you alleviate the care of each weak part of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes' veins
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	are red veins that are covered above the oil, and take away from the sight their work and weaken the oil always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, the work is first that you look at this oil, in which those veins are, and outside, and there is no other disease besides that one; then the work in such a way: command the patient to put his head in your healthy place, then suspend those veins all around according to their wisdom, and let the threads be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two openings made in one breast according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then gently apply those veins subtly, and stop the blood flow an hour after another, until you can remove those veins far from the oil; and guard that you do not pierce the oil with points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very hot in your work so that you do not cover those veins; and when you have done this, distill green and red wine into the oil to corrupt what remains of the previous.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all the blood in that hour, then apply a plaster on top of the oil with things that ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some time until the pain is eased and it is ensured that there is no abscess, then continue according to this method as long as it is safe; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror calls this "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with fire and medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then you must cut into the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is revealed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is revealed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then you should remove all the instruments that are in its form; it is called "rough head", and it should be made of iron from the same place as the original, and it should not be pointed like a lime as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place above the broken bone of the limb, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you feel that corruption is removed; and do this once, then restore the broken bone with drying agents.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is swollen, and there is heat in the body, and the body of the bone is swollen, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not recover and is not healed, and no bad accidents come, remove it when it is healthy; if not, there is no other remedy than to return the fistula to the opening of the sinus according to this form: and you should uncover the bone the second time by fire, and by wetting agents, and when it goes out uncovered, take the foret according to this form, and let the iron be at three angles, and let the fust be attenuated just to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it above the bone of the arm, and keep your hand away from the oil and the needle, then turn the forearm until it pierces the bone and you feel the pain because if he holds his hand on his elbow; and when the limb has been treated with dry medicines as I have indicated, and when the char heals and the bones harden, then apply the matter to the elbow; it is a lighter thing for the pain.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the end of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open wide and do not close, and it does not dislocate at the elbow, then you must bandage the pain; then clean it, then apply leeches or a heated poultice to draw out the pus, then put on the oil mixed with acid, aloe, incense, and sarccol, and then strain the oil and apply it with bandages and cloths; the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths that are soft enough, double them into fourths, and place one on top of the other according to the quantity needed; then strain it through a durable cloth, and start again with the leeches to draw out the pus without hurting; then remove the leeches and let the oil stay on for day and night, and if the swelling does not disappear, it is necessary to strain it well; then remove the poultice after the next day and night, and if you see the oil return to its original state, it is good; if not, start again with the bandages, cloths, poultice, and leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	forced detachment of a vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the vein, then open it, and come out with forceps like a piece of resin, and is easily seen; if you see it covered, the work is such that you drive a needle into the root of the part below this above, then drive another needle or double the thickness of the part of the arm; and pierce it, and let the first needle according to its position; then cover the part of the double thread with the skin, and hold it firmly, then remove the needle and put fresh oil on the wound, and leave it until the thread has healed with the vein, then care for the wound with comforting things until the wound is healed; and never cover the wound with a piece of cloth from each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear greatly displaced, prick them with a fine needle that comes from under the oil, and draw out the moisture and wipe the eyelids, and enter thus immediately; then extract it as much as is necessary to make them healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the spoon of oil
