Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing more than a drop of oil that is assembled in the oil, resembling a sharp descending arrow, and this is not really sharp; and the way of its appearance in the work is such that you make the patient sit with the evil above the seat, and straight, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move the mover until you see the drop coming up to your eyes; then it should be finished, and not wiped off and not dissolved, and see the things as they were; and if it does not descend, it is not arranged as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you let the pain rest between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make it over the corneal thread and the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal thread and the crown, until the arrow is out; and when it is out, then pour hot oil mixed with honey or mustard boiled and honey, then be cured of other cures until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the hot oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have similar cases in the division, and what is needed to pierce; if it works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the pain rest between your hands crossed, outside of the light for the sun, and with the healthy oil and pressed very tight; then put the paper of the oil to your right hand if the eyes are on the left, or to your left hand if the eyes are on the right; then take in your right hand if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called «almagda», or in your left hand if the eyes are on the right; then put the point of the instrument over the crown by the thickness of a hair in that part of the oil that is in the blind spot of the eye, then press the instrument called «almagda» vigorously, and restore your hand as long as it pierces into the part of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda is at the beginning of the space that is from the gold to the end of the needle; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal thread, and then put the instrument above or the hot oil.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he feels sharp pain now, he sees the hairs in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, and if the sharp pain returns, put the feather with the instrument, and when it is well secured and does not rise, gently twist slightly around your hand back and forth; then put a little cotton on the eye and leave it inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put in place the eye drop or some soft cloth soaked in red wine and plenty of honey, and tie it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those who are from our own group, put on top with plenty of honey.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard eyes, then you must use the tool called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Therefore pierce only the conjunctive, and do not move it too much in the front, but make the eye subtle, then beat the hardness, as we have said; and at the completion of the work compare to the pain that arises, in which it sleeps on its back in the dark place; and be careful of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and be tied according to its disposition just after this day; then release him in this same dark house, and examine his vision, and see some things, and then return the thread just after six days; and it is not necessary that you make the cure now, but it is necessary that you raise him, because the sharp increase is quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come, you should apply warm oil before the seventh hour, and it should be rubbed with what appeases the abscess; and when it is appeased, remove the cloth and place on its face a cold compress to cover any opening, and let it stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then gradually increase the time spent outside and convert it into its usual activities; and make sure that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Some came to us who were in the Yrach, who told us that in some countries people often cut themselves with sharp instruments, because of which the wounds become infected, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I read about it in books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of amalgams, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are made of pure tin.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the main part of them is of the same fineness, and the other in three angles ash.
de la char sor le neis	of the herb for the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never do noses or nostrils bear different amalgams, because there are some that seem like scorpions at the tip of the nose; and if there is such an amalgam or it has a dark color, and if the amalgam has a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those amalgams that are good and not enhanced, it is necessary that you make the pain between your hands against the sun; and work its nostrils, and pour the liquid of those amalgams, and take them out; because it is enough that you can hold in the thin and sharp substance of one part, until you know that that amalgam is all dissolved.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is nothing left that can be removed, then open it with all the subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if it is a pus-filled abscess, wipe it clean as it should be; and if it is malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize it until the wound is not stained and all the pus is removed. Then pour out or rinse with warm water and vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If it does not open and moisture comes into the palate, make sure it is healthy; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, make sure there is a bone in the jaw above, because the instruments do not come out to cut: therefore, you must go with a thin piece of linen, and hold it with both hands, and leave space between each nut as much or little; and put the painful teeth of the thread in its gum to the side, and pull out as far as it comes through the jaw inside the mouth; many times they do this with children at school, and it is an easy thing for someone who wants to do it; then hold the jaw that comes out of the jaw with one hand, and the other jaw that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and make them as we are who are or thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you see that they have not corrupted that part of the flesh, then remove the filth, soak in salt, and wash the thread in an Egyptian method, and put it back in its place as before; do this three times or more, until the thread has eaten away everything that remains of the flesh; and then put a plaster on the wound for several days until it is healed, and if there is need of drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, by which one distills oils and medicines into the wound:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or tin, resembling an open lamp, like a dog, and conduct it thus; and if you see, if make a closed dog, and it is the instruments plain to purge the head; and have one hand at the head for holding when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	for the sinew of the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a disease arises at the head of the neck that is called "telul", and grows and becomes large over time; and for this reason it is necessary to cover it at the beginning, and remove all the bone, then put the cautery or the burning medicine on the wound; and if it is difficult to cover it until it is large, if it is hard, of poor color, and has poor sensation: if you do not touch it with iron because it is an abscess, for when it is covered once, great harm comes to the pain; and if the abscess is softly touched, not with poor color, and you see that it can be completely covered, then remove the pain and the covering without fear, and cure the wound of similar and restrictive things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the bone is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	If solutions of continuity come from one of these cartilages, it is of little use, since in any man.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, if the wound is fresh and full of blood, and then the lips are sewn together at a seam, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already decayed on one side and the other, then you must scorch all the parts of their edges until they heal, then bring together both lips at a seam, and bind them, and powder with powder of dragon’s blood, and broken incense; and put the powders on a piece of strong or other plaster, and let it soak through him, then treat the wound until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of the stitching is such that you gather the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the abdomen; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes there are abscesses inside the lips, hard and small or large; therefore it is necessary to turn out the lips, and cut across each part, and take the pincers and scrape in every part; then fill the wound after the incision with ground glass broken, until the wound is no longer bleeding; then apply a poultice of bran, and cure the wound of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the teeth gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	often appear above the gums charred, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is necessary to hold it with pincers, and cover its root, and let the blood or the pus flow; then put on the tooth vitriol crushed, or other powders that are astringent and desiccants; and if this char returns after the incision, and often does, then cover it again, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments to cover.
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scars that are ugly and sharp; and sometimes they are black and yellow and green, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are black and smelly; it is necessary to place the bad breath between your hands, and its teeth should be in your holy, and remove the teeth or the scars that appear, until nothing remains; and thus make the black and green, and yellow and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if what is taken at the first level, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the tool, until you have removed everything; and wipe off that the teeth have business with various forms of instruments to remove, because the tool that removes them from under the teeth has other shapes than those that remove between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when treating a toothache that you delay pulling it as long as possible, for no one should do this; for it is a substance very high and therefore we have no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the pain is constrained to pull, then you must be certain of the tooth wailing.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the tooth is relieved, and one must be careful that it is not a holy tooth, and pull the good tooth; and all the time do not let the pain depart until the evil is extracted, for we have already done this to these saints; and when you are certain of the aching tooth, then you must burn around the tooth at all points; then move it with your fingers or subtle forceps at first and first, until it is well dislodged, then firmly fix the forceps; and let the patient hold the pain in their holy place between their teeth, and keep it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After straightening the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump back into place, take one of these tools and gently push it into each part lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is cracked and damaged, it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the pulps are; and if the straightening is subtly with nails, that it does not break when being straightened; and it is very important to cover around the gum to relieve the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and that a part remains, and again give the pain by the greater evil of the root more severe pains from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act in such a manner as the ignorant sainors do, who, by their haste and boldness, break the chariot at once, and never bring back what we have told; but they bring forth once upon a time through the root of this great disease because of the roots that they delay, or because of the chariot that they break, as often as we have seen; and when the dense is drawn, if blood comes out, which often happens, then use the wound with wine or vinegar and silk; and if it does not stop, then use the wound with vitriol broth; and if it does not work, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, by which one moves the first tooth, should be long pointed and large handed, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be large bodies so they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of good iron, and they should be sharp to hold the tooth.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulling, then you must put a soft cotton ball on the tooth to hold it.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	so that the tooth is softened, then push the pliers called "alligator", of which the patient seems like a beak; and they should be made inside like a lime and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not want to come out at all these needles, then it is necessary that you dig around the root completely, and put the instrument called "althali", which is a spatula, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be both large and thick so that it does not break easily, and if the root jumps out of the ground, it is good; if not, with all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument that has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before in the region of the teeth, and with this instrument that looks like large needles, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And these instruments are used except that they cannot break, and many of them are made of dense materials; and also other instruments, which I do not count; and the wise masters find their own instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach the use of an instrument due to the diversity of them and if they have broken the chariot or other bones, or if it hurts, if they seek the instruments that they need, as I have said, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well holding to hold the bone, that it not escape, but it can hold and remove; then restore the limb of medicines fitting for this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, if the doctor has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course, and the shape is ugly, and specifically in young women, it is necessary that you remove if the tooth is not aligned after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and no one can be made or smoothed: then the ray; and if it is with the tooth, take this instrument that is like a small beak, and is similar to a sharp iron in some:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper pot slowly and slowly in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that you can remove it, then the lime from one piece of lime as follows is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the lime of which one makes the arrows; and in lime the tooth slowly and slowly in your hands gently, so that it does not move until it crumbles; then the plane at the end to any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, then you must remove the roughness as long as it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth ache
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth in front ache, or by percussion or falling, and the pain cannot be relieved by pressing on the gums to prevent them from grinding, and you treat them with restrictive medicines, it does not work; then you must use a gold wire, because silver wire becomes green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are close together, take the wire and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the affected tooth between the healthy ones, as many times as necessary, until you can feel wisely against the healthy tooth on the other side; then start the covering again from the part where you started, and gently and skillfully press your hand, until it does not move; and let your fingers be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then, tie the loose teeth with a thin thread to a needle, and gather them together, and place them between the healthy tooth and the gum, so that it does not bleed the tongue; then leave it tight as long as it can hold, and if it slips out, or the thread breaks, then tie it with another thread; if it holds, it will serve in this way for a long time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the filling of the two healthy teeth, and the two missing ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth breaks, if it is reset in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and does not interfere with any that is wise and suffering, and is never made into the shape of a cow's tooth, and it is placed in the place of the defect, and it is tied on as we have said, and holds, and serves in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tongue's ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is this ligament that comes from the tongue or naturally, which one should cut in such a way as to open the mouth of the wound, and hold the head in its place, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or no outlet, and it is from a deep wound, if you boil the linen and cut widely, gently; and be careful that the wound is not too large, for the artery that is outside; and when you have done, lift the tongue with a sponge of rose or cold water, then place a tent of linen on the tongue every night, so that the wounds cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If there is bleeding from the vein, put vinegar on the wound; and if it does not stop, then cauterize it with a slow-burning fire brand, which is good for the skin; then treat the wound with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see that the wound is of a dark or black color and hard, and the patient does not feel pain, do not touch it, for it is chancre; and if it is inclined to suppurate and there is moisture, pour water through a thin spout, and deliver from both sides; and if it does not stop bleeding at your work, put vinegar on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you have removed all the blood; then lift up the wound with silk and cotton, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	There are no abscesses in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called the II mandibles, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, then be careful: if it is an abscess hard of small size and of yellow color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the running of blood; but leave it until it is soft, and then you will break it open, or it will break by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is thin, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first check if the abscess has calmed down and is quiet.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then place the painful part in front of the sun, and its joint should be in a straight position, and the worker's mouth and the sergeant's hand between his hands, and press the tongue away from all the instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be of silver or thin brass like some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the needle and the hook in the amber, and draw it out above as much as you can; and take nothing from the cloth with it, then cover the instrument, of which this is the form, that seems like forceps; and the chief are bent, and one end is sharp, and very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use a pair of pliers, with which it has the following form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And on one side, it is sharp, and on the other side, blunt; and when you have removed one of the arrows, remove the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sharp parts with hot, sharp, and salty water, and if blood comes out, gargle the sharp parts with hot water, or crushed pomegranate skins, or wormwood, and similar things, until the wound is clean; then cure it as much as possible; and never other abscesses come out of the throat except the two arrows, so remove them in the same way as the two arrows.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was swollen inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and she had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe or eat or drink, and died if she remained like this for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had been punctured twice through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore quickly and inserted it into the one nostril, then removed the pus through the other nostril, and a large portion of blood; then I refilled it again through the other nostril, and pressed the tongue against the mouth; afterwards, I inserted the needle into this abscess, and sucked out a part, and did not remove any more than a small amount of blood; and thus the woman was able to breathe again, and began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at this abscess for a long time; the abscess kept growing back, and filled up the cavity that I had emptied, so that it became very large; therefore, I inserted and cauterized it inside her throat: thus she did not grow any more; and I left these parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When applying to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not too large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, and you see that the patient's abscess is calm, and it is subtle, then you must cover it; and the one that is round and not too long; and if it is bloody or dark red, then you must avoid incision of the li.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger over the pain.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the method that I have mentioned, of its blench and length, you should make the hairs sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned earlier; then cut the opening in the eye, and remove it, and treat it with one or two of the instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two arrows.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you only cover the excess which is outside of the natural limit; for if you cover more, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have mentioned in the incision of the two arrows, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pain is too severe, then it is necessary to use an engine for the cauterization of the sensitive area.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts his head on your sound shoulder, and then presses his tongue against the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cauterization, and confis with very hot water, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and by the movement of this instrument, which is in the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the patient has a hair or something to put the medicine on, like the movement of a spoon, and puts the instrument all the medicine over the wound; and the patient lies down on his side, so that the saliva and the mucus flows from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not drip to the throat and the blood; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it over the wound, for a quantity of half an hour, until you see the benefit and the medications of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and blow the instrument all the cotton into the wound above, until the cotton is burned over the wound; and do this often, until the cauterization of the medicine is perfect, then let it dry for four or five days, and if you have the ability to start again with the cauterization of the medicine, and start again, and after the cauterization, smear it around the wound with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be wrapped in hot water, and be treated with gargles until they are healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more saved from the incision than from the cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take chamomile and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and similar herbs, and put them all or some of them in a pot, and put honey in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot have an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or lead, and it should be one of the prongs stuck in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the boil through the nose, until the boil is dead; afterwards, do it repeatedly until the boil dries, and make sure you do not apply this at the beginning of the onset of the abscess chaut, for many things happen; and do not make this unless at the decline of the abscess chaut.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cloth and put it inside the head, so that the tongue does not stick out too much; for the cloth does not make the vapor heavy on the tongue, and it is good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is found in the throat or fish bones or nothing; therefore you must take out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun at all instruments, so that you can see the thing; and what does not open itself and is returned to the throat, you must make vomit the bad thing as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if the thing is stuck by vomiting; or the bad things swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to the string, and then swallow it; and when it comes back to the throat, it will stick, and then pull out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take the instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the crooked instruments should be curved to the head so that they can more easily enter the throat, and the head should be raised high; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that the whole does not come, or do not push the bone inside; and it is better that the hairs push the instrument, for it is softer or the thing is as such; if it goes down, or it pulls the entire instrument evenly, as far as it is full.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat sinew
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	The throat sinew is not medicine, as I said in the division, by the care of medicines; and if it does not help, then look at the hairs in the throat to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinew, then it is to be cut with a small knife, or with sharp needles that are equal to the size of a needle.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if the needle does not work, then take a hair from your head, and push it into the wound of the sinew, then push or move the hair with the sharp iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the wound is infected throughout the day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in the direction of swallowing, and move it to your hand often; and when the sinew feels the cold, then it breaks.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	If it does not stain as we have said, then smoke the wound with asafetida, using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will stop without scarring.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The way of the fumigation is that you hold a pot or vessel with charcoal in it, and place a cover over it perforated in the middle, and in this puncture place the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and put the wound at the end of the tube in its mouth, and close its mouth, so that the fume does not escape but goes directly to the wound; and the wound will now heal, and if it does not, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salted things and others, and do not drink water; and thus it is necessary that the wound heals by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the jaw, so that when it can be seen, it resembles a crowbar to enter the throat; and it has the appearance of a care beak, and there is roughness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot slip.
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what the memory comes after one and another in this book, and they differ in puncturing and cutting; and it is in two ways that one is in its own shape itself, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for those who are at the waist.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Because the abscesses of the chief are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the elbow are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the boil is completely dead; and if there are such as it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die immediately after their completion, like abscesses that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	Because when abscesses come beyond joints, and it is left until it is swollen all around, perhaps the tendon and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which it is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is located away from the main limb, and if you delay perforation until it dies, it will harm the main limb; or if it is located away from the base, if you pierce it too soon, it will kill; and it should only be pierced when the abscess has been crushed and digestion is completed, except for that which is located away from the base, so it cannot protrude and remain alongside, and a fistula forms; and it cannot be healed in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary to remove the pus from the perforation of the abscess that has died according to the completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and the swelling, and the lessening of the debatement and the lessening of the main part of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary to make the perforation lower down the limb where the pus is most apparent; and let the perforation be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is near the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all these places equally where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the affected limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the limb, it is better to leave the incision until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you prick it beforehand, the blood vessel of the limb will follow along with it, and it is stained with much dirt; and perhaps the lips harden and pierce through it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is pricked according to the wide blood vessel, as the limb has need of it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary to treat small abscesses with small incisions; and large abscesses with large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses or it is necessary to cover the wound, and to cover; when it has become as soft as cloth, and is softened, then it should be done as one does with bedsores: and if there are such abscesses that are cut in three angles, and if there are such abscesses that are covered like the fleece of wool, as abscesses of arrows; and if there are such abscesses where a round cut is made, and other shapes and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who do not have a head, if the abscess is superficial, it is necessary to lance it completely; and if the abscess is large, and has great swelling, and you lance it, if you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but only a part; then stop the abscess on the other side, then take away nothing else; do this repeatedly, until all the pus is drawn out; especially if the wound is of weak strength, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the experienced never test once with the outflow of the pus, that by chance the wound may die, and you do not lose it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, dry the wound, and check if the abscess wound is small; and if a tailor complains, soothe him with tents of linen or woolen cotton; and if there are large abscesses, and much pus, it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have pulled it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shreds of linen without moisture, and bind it close to the wound; then open, and treat the dressing as long as they are healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood clots occur in your work, apply sharp cold and wet compresses, and gently wipe the clot, and put it on the affected area repeatedly for many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood clots persist, apply proper treatment and care, and the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is too tense or if the wounds are very painful, it is recommended that you put on tents and wipe with dampened cloths in wine and oil; and if it is in a state of inflammation, and the wounds are charred, it is recommended that you put on dampened cloths in cold and oil, or in cold and oil mixed with vinegar, as we have said; then drain the abscess and dress and treat, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what must be understood universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the head, and there are ways of us that are in threads, as is the case of a surgeon's needle, and many more like it.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also large and such ones that have moisture like chickens; and there are some that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery is not against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the belly is such that you try every tool called "entromissoire", from which the shape comes after, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, it makes it through the long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off the hair that contains that moisture, for it returns when one leaves nothing; then plunge cotton in Egyptian oil, if present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it there the next day; and this will prevent what remains overnight.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, as before, the second day, and the third, with the cotton, until you know that it will not remain overnight; then treat the wound with ointment, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess does not open easily, then cut it according to this form, long; and pour in your ointments, and scrape off all the skin, and put all your care into drawing out the pus from where it is. And if the artery makes it against you, do as I have told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same if the abscess is pierced, and cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And if the cut is above the abscess, it is lighter, for they are not deep.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if to any of these abscesses or boils there is no moisture, and of these was the abscess that I copied or from an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a rough, rough, and white stone, and could not be broken; and if one had tried to cut it, it would have made just as bad a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or from the boils, those that come from the head of children and from the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the most dependent part, to let the pus out; and treat them as it is fitting.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	often have abscess in the neck, and they are dislodged, and they are inflamed, and sometimes come from other parts of the body, and they are very painful, and they are intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly in its own side, as with the neck and the abscess of the jaw, as we have said; and the similarities of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are also harmful ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one which you see of good disposition in the chest, and it is similar to the color of the heart, and it does not move from any part and is not attached to the neck or the artery or the vessel, and it is not deeply buried; then it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape all parts, and place the two lips of the wound as one, if you have skill, as we have said in abscesses of the jaw; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and do not make a spouting wound, which the hands may escape, and do not look too early, before you cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not stop bleeding, put in the wound vinegar broth, or some powders that stop blood, and close the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is softened, and then begin to apply a poultice.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is clean, return to your work, until you complete it; then ask your guide whether there remain any small scabs, and cut and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is much blood in the root of the scab, then it does not matter that you cut that scab at its root, but tie it with a double-strength thread, and let it drip through it without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian oil, then heal.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire pus, it is necessary that you gather the two lips of the wound and hold them together, then since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the pus.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you cover the root of it and pull out forcefully, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those pus-filled abscesses that contain excess, pierce where it is most likely to die; and pierce in this way, hanging down, then apply compresses and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well dressed, if the ointment heals, apply char and keep it until it is healed.
de squinance	of dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and said of the throat-cutter; but I never saw one in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have dislocation, the cut of the neck which is called "epiglottis" must be avoided; and this is because all the veins and the pore of the evil are in those who have abscess full in the mouth, or in the neck or in the throat.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the pore of the mouth, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it out in three circles or four, with a small incision across between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision through the surface of the cartilage; and these are suitable for the section of the epiglottis so that there is no harm, and the vessels are long and do not bleed.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is not skilled, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the neck all around, then cuts the cartilage until it comes to the chain; and avoid the veins of blood, if you see anything, and then cover the surface, as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the stream of the chain that springs forth from the limb that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which one doubts strangulation, gather both lips of the wound together, and tie it all around without the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce heat until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this as long as the throat is completely stiff, and the limbs are judged to be dead, and the defect causes the arm to fall.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, one should pierce the epiglottis because the limbs cannot support it, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and because they ordered the ancient ones to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease had passed, and it had passed in three days or four.
