And therefore, they commanded to sew the wound and cure it, as long as it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not coughed blood nor bled through the throat, the blood came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened and closed the wound, and cured it so that it was healed; and she did not suffer harm except that she had a weak voice, and she returned to her usual state; for I believe that in the tissue of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in the color of a goose, and is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; or naturally without cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental way is in two ways, one of which is similar to a large goose, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us through an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be opened except by a skilled surgeon, and he should examine and search throughout the entire abdomen: if you find it as I have described, and cannot be cut at all, then cover it with a bandage, just like we do with the others, and remove it completely if there is any; and look for it quickly, and treat it as it should be, until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	For the fire cauterization
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways we do, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary for me to tell the whole difference between us and the issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the issue is chills and fever lasting, until the boils have passed, and is accompanied by the purging; then the fever and chill rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With ours there is no chill or fever or pain, and it contains the pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a small grain, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, whether dry or moist, and much of color is as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat a new patient, to first test and inquire about the "entromissoire" instrument, according to the form of the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you press or moisten the least dry part of the abscess that you pierce, and return your fingers slowly and slowly, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the "entromissoire", and be careful that it does not slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	When moisture runs through a cut, which color it has, make it as I said for the other abscesses; and if afterwards the wound does not come moisture, scrape off the fat, then make a cross on it, and take pincers, and scrape lightly from every part and wipe the coat or where you take it that you take it clean with the knife; and if you cannot take it clean, then tear it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if nothing remains, it often returns to us; and if it stays for a while without bothering you, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders, and hold the wound, and put on top of things that calm abscesses, and treat other treatments until it is healed; and if the wound is large, then cut out both lips of the wound, and treat what is injured.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	If you see that it is against you or another, if it hurts and fills the wound with broken glass, and leave it for two or three days until the wound heals, and rest the bleeding of the blood; then return to the copper that was left.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See the shapes of the instruments for puncturing, and there are three ways: large and medium and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three ways: large, medium, and small, to extract the abscesses of fistula; and they are like the arrows that one buys for the pots, and are made of gold, or iron, or silver, and are worth as much as those that are yellow, and are more expensive because of their black point to extract the fistula pus; and they are three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of nails are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are nails that have two prongs in three ways; and there are nails that have three prongs, and they are also of three ways; and there are nails that have two prongs, and a single prong nail, and they are of three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The main purpose of these tools is to cut, and there are some that only cut in one direction, from which we scrape the skin, because we do not want to cut the vein or nerve; and among these scrapers are the almels placed in maniches, so that the pain does not persist at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are used only in one place, such as legs, arms, breasts, and angles, and similar places; and never made any other tool small, resembling scorers of pustules, according to this form, with which we drain blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is put on no healthy skin that can cover veins, and arteries, and once again it forms according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	No one should inflate the breasts of men when they begin to rot, as if they were the breasts of women; and they remain deformed and swollen, and whoever wants to heal them, it must be according to this form of this line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with medicine made of char, then stitch together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and heal it until it is healed; and if the breast sinks down, and is softened for its greatness as it is in women, and make it into two pieces above, by similar cuts; so that one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the largest line contains the smallest according to this form, of this line .b. up to .g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not made completely, because the pain does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with moistened cotton in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it melts the remaining fat, then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the knees
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the knees are ways of hard scrofula where there are lumps, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply old cotton to the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat with ointment suitable for this as long as it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, then do as we have said about puncturing scrofula, and if the wound remains open, then cauterize it as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the tearing of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is torn, and the flesh above it is sound, then often abscesses occur, and also there is blood flowing from the vein and abscess; and if one knows this to be due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and even; and if you feel it, it is with tension; and if it is due to the vein, then they are round and less numerous; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is outside the bones and angles and collarbone and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the use of iron, and the one who is at the head should also avoid it, and in the one who is swollen from an artery fleeing through the long skin; then open the belly as much as possible, and tear the artery from the cloth until it is exposed; then insert a needle on the other side, and pierce it with another needle on the other side, and tie the artery with double silk according to what I have indicated in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then do not remove the skin between the two belts of an intromission until the one that is there is gone, and remove the abscess; then treat the cure that you have mentioned as long as the wound heals; and if the abscess is for the belly of the vein, if it is necessary to stain your hand with what comes from the abscess on all the skin, then remove the needle from the skin that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and there should be double silk so that you can pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have indicated to you or with the thread of one of the two parts of the needle; and if you doubt that the thread does not come out, then put another needle all along the thread of the first needle, and tie the threads in four strands; then cover the abscess until the superfluous part is gone, then cover the wound and leave what is left; then put a moist cloth on the wound with wine and oil, then treat the cures of tents and ointments as long as it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses come to the arteries and veins, abscesses also come to the neck when it is cut, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And these often occur in the joints and in all parts where there are joints, and this is great pain, and its color resembles the color of blood, and it is in many different positions with pain; and when it is stretched, if the patient feels pain, and it does not look like blood, but rather from outside the body; and it moves from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor up or down, and those who are in joints do not need to be covered with iron: perhaps there is contraction; and those who are at the neck or face, making the skin wrinkled.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, tie it with needles at its base; and if it is large, hang it from the tip, scrape it, then remove the bone and stitch the wound at the seam, and care for it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	large, hanging tumors
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There are no cases in the belly and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots and large heads; and there are both small and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two or three bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were always moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one XVIII ounces heavy, and in the other VI З., and in the work of the incision is that you look if the hairs are moist, and the color of the artifact is white and moist and of subtle root; if the copper has a wide span, and they are in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting often brings too great corrosion of blood, and if you see the hair escaping and fearful of the incision of the iron, take a strong thread well made, and tie the artifact as we have said, and leave it for two days; then restrain, and do not stop stretching the thread through the artifact until it covers the artifact, and cut through it with labor; and if the roots are large, use the copper itself on the belly, but you must carefully cover the half, then cauterize that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cover the thread which is of pale color and poor sense and of little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these are abscesses that have become infected, and I will come to the treatment of chancres here afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is suppurating
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the suppuration comes from the cauterization of a wound or a cut in the face, and it is on the belly and among some of the pus, as it has in other wounds, or blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or pus; and if it is from the rupture of the face and from the issue of the feces, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it to its sides, it returns, and perhaps if it is torn, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for much work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a simple matter, and it opens well when one presses it with the hand, without too much constraint; and if it is for an abscess, it is large and hard, and it is attached to a quantity; and if it is for windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the appearance of the work indicates whether it is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary to leave the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, as I have told you or in the chapter on arrows.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it appears to be for the intestine or the boil, then command the patient to dye his linen, and let it extend straight all around, then sign around the belly; then place the injured part between your hands, then wrap the half of the abscess above the large intestine; then tie it with a strong silk cord tightly, and let the other end be loose; then open the half of the abscess extended over the cord, and insert your finger, and remove the intestine; if you find the cord, cut it, and remove the intestine from the lower part of the belly; and if you find the boil, take it at the base, and scrape away the excess; and if the artery or vein causes you to go against it, then go around it carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two threads, and cut the two needles where you have pierced; then stretch the abscess in four parts over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the part as long as it can bear, and let the dead flesh die by itself; or you can remove it when it has become thin and ready to fall off, then treat the wound as we have said; and extract the pus or moisture that you have found, then treat the part as it needs, and suture the abscess.
dou chancre	For the fire cauterization, instruct
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	For the fire cauterization, instruct
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the procedures, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge once the hairs of black bile; then make it clean if it has manifest repletion, then wipe the hair and skin of good flesh to perform the procedure; then pour your instruments or cauterization, and the hair from all parts, and the skin from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and wipe well the place with your hand or something, and if the bleeding does not stop, do not make the incision of the artery or vein, if you cauterize until the wound is dry; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already spoken in the previous division about the resemblances of dropsy, and how the assembly of the swelling is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the treatment by medicines, and that which is treated by fire: if it is only swollen; and one should not touch fire in these two resemblances: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarche, for it is a deadly matter; therefore when you treat this resemblance of dropsy which is called "swelling" by medicines, and the treatment does not work, if you look at whether the pain is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, as vomiting and similar things; then do not touch fire, for there is doubt; and if you see the pain of great virtue, and he has no other disease except dropsy alone, and he is not too young or too old, then thus: gently lift the pain upwards with your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the swelling to the lowest part of the worst, then take the spatula in this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let the incision be of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let the incision be pointed, and ensure that no part is too deep so that it can reach the intestines when cutting, and it cannot bleed; then check if there is dropsy near the intestines: if it is necessary to make a second incision three fingers' breadth from the navel on the left side; and if it is for the disease of the liver, then the incision should be on the right side of the navel three fingers' breadth; and if it is for the miuce, then it should be on the left side, and it should not be necessary that the hairs grow over the incision so that the superfluous do not run to the weak liver; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push, and remove your hand from all the space between the skin and the flesh as if scraping at a quantity of an inch or around; then pierce the flesh until the space reaches the desired length, and that is the length of the blade, then remove this instrument with this shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and is made of light rain or iron, and has a small opening at one end; and on the other side, three openings; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head of the shoulder is slit as with a pen, and that is the form of the incision that the scribes make the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of the instrument is the awl, so that when the instrument comes to the skin, then descend now above the instrument; voiding the half or the third part, because if you void more than it is necessary in that hour, by chance if the patient dies from the resolution of his spirit from the arm, or he faints, or he approaches death; but in voiding according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the wound mean, and its thorns; then withdraw the instrument and retain the skin, and it is retained now for the one who stops the opening that is above the syringe, of which I have spoken, that you perforate in this manner; then start the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient suffering as, and take from the skin a small quantity; do this every day, and guard against following too long until it is only a little blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the pain, and you let it be very severe, then the cure of the sepulture or sand bath, and much sweat or bath and in the sun, and if it becomes infected from drinking; and the cure of desiccative medicines until it is healed, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the splinter, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the insertion of the staff
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever is born without a pustule in the staff, or the pustule is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to prick at all times with a very fine needle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place or puncture the very fine thread of silk, and tie it and keep it in this way for three days or four, and when it wants to urinate, if it can be opened, urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it does not suit, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is punctured is small, it is treated with a very fine thread of silk, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the puncture in their limb are blind, because no one is born with the puncture at the tip of the penis, so that they cannot urinate before their penis reaches the top; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the marriage, and it is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the work is such that the hairs lie so often on their backs, the head of the knife and the handle are like the size of a pen, so that the punctured wound is in the middle, as it should be; and guard against the evacuation of blood which often comes, and if it does, use the same cloth to stop the bleeding.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the knife
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often come pus blisters in the knife, and it is an appearance of a bad wound; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; if you prick them at the tip of the knife, and wrap and clean all, then put on a moist cotton bandage in Egyptian method; then the treatment of the wound continues until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if it is a malignant ulcer, with putrid color and foul odor, then you must cauterize it with fire.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have scraped it, and if the ulcer is deep within the skin and has parts inside and outside, then you must first remove the part that is inside; and when it is cleaned, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, do not be sure that the wound is not pierced, and if it becomes darker and more corruption in its wound and where the coion; then remove everything that is black and corrupted, then apply the ointment made of honey and flour which is made of grape skins and walnuts, then treat other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding comes from a wound, then treat the lunar cauterization as follows:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterization helps in two situations: when bleeding occurs and when the wound is corrupted. If the tailbone is corrupted and retracted, then you should apply a cloth soaked in urine to the affected area and urinate on it; if the skin has not been circumcised, or if it is a wound or an abscess, then you should scrape it with a sharp instrument until the tissue is loosened and freed from all parts of the tailbone; if this is a difficult task, then you should scrape it with a sharp instrument at the head of the tailbone and the surrounding area, then apply a subtle dressing of linen moss in cold water, so that it does not recur.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not different from other wounds; therefore, when we perform this work of our will, and properly in children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen the majority of masters and experts who performed circumcision around the age of one year, and in force, and at all times; if it was the case that one of them covered the glans penis and delayed the other from above.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	And the recovery is slow, and the pain is doubled, and the wound healing which is done by chance often escapes the point of the member; and the healing of the joint may escape and corrupt the work, and many times it happens that they are born thus without need of healing and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the healing which is done by force to all the member of the limb I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally in all the thickness; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and the method of the first work is that you make the child think, if he listens, that you do not tie the thread only around the stick so much, and then throw the force between your hands or outside your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then close your hand on the stick and blow gently, and take it up as high as the end of the stick is; then clean the dirt that is gathered, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it away from one limb to another; and hold it between two fingers by the second work at the pouch and the correct index, and cover between the two limbs, then lift the breath quickly and take the head of the stick; then let the blood flow slowly and slowly, for that is the most dangerous; and put powder on top and on top of the powder a piece of glue from a piece of fresh meat cooked with rosewater, confected with rose oil and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and treat the other cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of forces for the mummification is such: the two heads should be tense and sharp, and the heads should be equally large:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mummification is when the cut is too deep at the incision; therefore, it is necessary to extend it to your angle, similarly with the copper, and if you cannot hold it at your angle, then hold it with pliers, and then the copper.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three hours, and what is outside the rod is inflated, let it remain until the abscesses are soothed, and scrape lightly; and if the copper as you can move, and guard from the part of the rod, it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the limb of things that have been wounded by powder wounds, which we have said to treat powders, and if one goes too far with care, it will not harm; therefore, treat them as we have said until they are healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the closure of a stone, or blood congealed, or bowel, or charred, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is high or close to the bladder, it is necessary that the hairs be pulled up over his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and his belly stretched from the part above the back, and the hairs restrained as much as possible; and thus the opening of the bladder is pressed against the stone above, for which reason the urine is released, and if it does not come, as we have said, and the hairs feel great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called «siringue», of which this is the form: and it should be made of thin silver hair, like the pen of an eagle; and it should be slender at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of the urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie the head of the linen or cotton to the chief of the tube, and blow the head of the thread into the tube; and fold the excess of the linen and blow it at the head of the tube, then oil the tube with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a stool, and the urine and the cloth moistened with oily oil and olive oil and vinegar; then press the tube firmly to the end of the tube, until it reaches the root of the tube, then double the tube upwards over the edge; then blow the tube before towards the cloth, and feel the patient coming towards the empty thing, and this is not made according to this order except by reason that the conductor or she goes twisted; then stop the thread at all the linen little by little, and the urine follows the linen, then extract it, and correct the urine; and start again the tube until the bladder is empty and aligned with the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When skin or blood comes into the bladder, and there is inflammation and assembly, and you see distillation of acids and medicines, then use all the instrument called «clepsedre», and it is the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the needles are passed through the part where the medicine cuts so that it does not touch the urethra too much, so that you can draw out the moisture, and put in whatever is necessary; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, put the head of the syringe into the moisture, and pull the piston which is outside; then draw the moisture into the syringe, and pump it strongly back inside; then the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the pain will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle catheter with which you catheterize the bladder: if it is in:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or iron, and is the highest part; and removed from the shoulder where the tendons are; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you see clisterizer the bladder, then lay it between the two breasts formed by a good double thread of wool, and heat the pooc of that moisture over the fire; then pour the head of the clistere into the rod, then strain your hand on the bladder all around the moisture, until the hairs feel that that moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and perforate it roundly; then pull the thread strongly in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles the dal, and put inside what you see oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it with the tool; and do as you have done with the bladder, press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of stones
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	In the division of the chapters, we have spoken about the ways of stones and their extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stones that are in the rain and all the signs, and in which stone one should open a hole; and in the bladder, and in the staff; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stones that are in the bladder often occur more frequently in children, and this is a sign that the sharp pain of the bladder resembles a sharp pain in its subtlety; and it opens harene, and causes great pain to the staff, and it happens many times, and then hardens; and at too many of these pains the foundations; and it is light for the healing of children up to the age of four, and it is very painful in old people, and is a constant complaint for those between young and old; and it is a lighter cure for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with ointment, to draw out all the matter that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never clogs up when trying to remove the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound by the feet, and stand up and move it away from the body, so that the stone descends to the edge of the bladder, and never goes up through the thigh; then sit it between your hands and prepare it, and your hands should be away from your thighs, so that the bladder is entirely descending downwards; then remove and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry to cut across the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she does not cry out at all, then gently press your right index finger onto the palm of her hand, if the pain is sharp, or in the middle, if the pain is dull; and apply it to the base, and strike with a stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then moisten the area where you see it cutting into the skin; then press upwards, and the blood will flow out where you see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the anus with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand over the testicles, and his left hand to remove the skin that is outside the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then cut the sponge, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And making between what is between the thighs and the foundation, not in the middle but on the right side of the naval; and it should be straight up the spine, and its tail should be at the foundation or the base, and its belly should be wide by deficiency, and inside it should be narrow, according to the quantity of the spine, not too large; perhaps the pressure that is at the foundation, that it should jump out without effort; and if there are pieces or angles, and margins: if it is gray to issue, and if there are pieces that are smooth, like a glass, and rounded, whose exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	When there are angles and margins in that place, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump, it is necessary to strain it with nails that are as thin as a lime at the top, for the stone to not escape; or you drive out of the instrument subtly curved at the top; and if you do not engage it thus, expand the little pouch, and if there is no decortication, then strain it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first take the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove the small ones, and the smaller ones afterward if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be made larger, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the wound: either it dies, or the urine comes out through the place where the bones cannot be healed; but nevertheless you must try to draw it out, or tear it with pincers, until you pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply incense, aloe, and dragon's blood to the wound, and bind it, and place a moist cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and vinegar and cold rosewater, to soothe the abscess; then replace the wound on its bone, and do not remove the bandage until the next day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, apply a lot of oil and vinegar to the joint, then treat with an ointment of honey and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes into the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and is retained by the urine, which is known to be held without leakage with the urine: then put your hand in the wound, and extract that clot, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder, and cause it to perish; then lift the wound with vinegar and salt and herbs, and help it in all ways that you can, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the remedies that you cure it with, that you tie both thighs together, and gather the medicines above the joint.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the arrow is small, and it is conducted by a rod, and tied up, and the urine cannot issue; then the cure for this that I have said before, that you cut many times, is to excuse the cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already experienced this.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron rod according to this form and be at three angles tied up in one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie the arrow around the rod outside of the bladder, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then gently push the iron rod into the rod until it reaches the arrow; and slowly turn the iron rod in your hand on the arrow, until you can pierce the arrow from the other side; then soon the urine will come out, then press your hand above where the part of the arrow that is inside the rod is.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is already broken, and it has jumped with the urine, and it is stuck to the hairs; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then pull the thread from below the stone and the other above, then make the rod in the middle of the stone between the two threads, then extract it, and remove the thread, and clean the clotted blood that is in the wound; and cure until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone from women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rare that stone occurs in women, and if it does occur once, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-dressed who will undress herself, specifically when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well versed in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that if the woman's stone is larger than the man's stone, it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear involved. And if necessary, you should send for a skilled midwife, and if you cannot find one, do not try to perform the operation yourself; instead, call a wise woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command regarding the examination of the stone; and look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary to place her on her back and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, she should push it out of her body, and recommend that she push it out or bear down with her right hand on her anus, forming a fist.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary to move it from great to great from the entrance of the anus until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut across the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the body, where it is muscle-filled, and feel the arrow in that part; and do not move her above the bone or below, and let the tailor make a small hole in the first place; then push the arrow through the hole in the belly until the arrow can come out, and know that there are many kinds of arrows: namely, small and large and sharp and blunt, long and round and rough and smooth, and those with rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to recognize the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if you do not know, put leeches on the wound, and keep them there for an hour until the wound is dry; then return to your work, until the stone is fully removed, and have tools that I have told you about in the extraction of the stone as helpers in your work; and if you do not know, and it is the artery that has been cut, put powder on the wound and bandages and bandages, and do not restart, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, for fear that the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound healed, return to your work until the stone is formed.
de hernie carnouse	for a hernia carnouse
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery ramice is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white faca, which is detached from the intestines, which contain the urine; and it is called «faca», and never properly in the thread of the urine, if one wishes that it is another urine; and this is the skin of the intestine between the white faca that we have said; and it does not have it unless there.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is from weakness that comes to compressions, and it is spread out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from blows to the compressions, and this moisture has many colors: or it is declining yellow to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or aquous white, and there are more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, it is the abscesses are, I poc long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the compressions, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own skin, it is the abscesses are with part of the egg, and because one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the compressions and the white asfac, then it feels good; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, try all the intermediary questions, from which its form was before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introducer, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary to clean the hairs according to as much power and the repletion of its body; then place it on its back, on something a little high, and cover it with much cloth; then lie on its left side, and command the minister to lie on its right, and extend the iron to one of the two ribs of the chest; then take the spatula and scrape the skin of the chest from the long end to above the wrist, and its edge straight in cutting the skin of the chest towards the white face, and scrape the skin subtly according to as much power; then pierce the white plain with a sharp and wide opening, and extract all the sharp, and then put your forceps, and fasten the white above; and do not touch the ribs of the chest, but only the white; scrape all or in pieces carefully the side of it subtly, if you do not scrape it well, it will return to the sharp; and if the vein springs up in your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white. Then gather the two flaps of the chest at one seam, then treat it as the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you have removed the broken bone that has been corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to bind the vessels that are suspended, in doubt of the flow of blood; then cover the wound with all the suspended, and extract the bone, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the bone is assembled in two parts together, it is because there are two branches; then cover the other part as you have done the first evenly, then suck out the blood, and put in the wound a poultice of rose oil; and put on top another poultice of wine and oil, and place over the two bandages, and tie it to the limb that is according to this form:
