Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and place them according to this pattern around the neck of the trousers, and one of them above the foundation at the back, and the other at the part of the elbow; and the other two at the two angles, and everything assembled is restricted in the loop of the trousers; and once this branch of the cautery is medicated in the shape of an iron tail, and it is that you take a sharp cauterizing instrument, and cut into the skin of the wounds, and heat it as we have said, so that the white pus that contains the poison is discovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and prick the pus with small incisions, and scrape the skin with this sharp cautery:

And in all ways that you can, until you remove everything; and beware that the knife does not touch the bone; and cleanse this work so that it is safer; and guard against bleeding, and avoid things that are harmful; and if anything goes wrong, such as an abscess or bleeding or other harmful thing, treat it according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the pain is severe and does not want to undergo this work due to its horror, then apply incision, as I have said, and when you are certain that the abscess is ready to be lanced, as we have indicated, place the pain on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess at the part farthest from all the soft tissue, and make the incision along the length of the body; and let the wounds be wide so that all the sharp edges are removed; then put cotton on the wound, and tie it, and leave it to drain the remaining sharp edge, then treat the wound until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the sharp edge to issue from the mouth of the wound, it is necessary that you insert a pen or the instrument used to treat the sharp edge of hydropikes, as its form has been indicated before; and enlarge the wound slightly, and let the sharp edge return, and gather after six months or within a few days, and when it is gathered as before, and thus the pain will pass its days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of abscesses in the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	There are many different positions that cause fear in more people, because it seems to me that moving is better than leaving it; and I will tell you the work and similar things about the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the groin and immediately from the thighs; and this is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known whether it comes from excessive aggravation and ague, which spreads in the groin, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the blood; and there is no pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and perhaps it is some gray, poor, and pus-filled abscesses, and of yellowish color, and sometimes comes from a vein, or from an inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by the lack of artery, then it is known by the position of the abscess being high, when you press it towards your fingers; and it should only be touched once.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are made of vein puncture are known by their position at the expression of gentle touching of the fingers, and can often make the cut above this resemblance, and above others; and you should check the care of the wounds, then lift the skin high, and pull out the thread from below the white surface, and deliver the suspended part of all parts of the skin.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the skin is already swollen with these needles, then it should be cut and cleaned; and if it is in the white surface, or inside the vessels, then it should be delivered completely, and cleaned roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the arrow's head is in the back, it is necessary that you remove it all, and extract the tip, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your surgeries are completed, apply the wound with a linen cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, then use other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess surrounded by a swelling similar to a hernia, with the softening of the groin, and the pain increases when it moves; and the treatment of this disease is just as difficult and dangerous as the previous one, and we will tell you the operation for it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to seat the painful part on an elevated seat, then lift the suspensory ligament of the tendons down to your fingers, and all the veins that are close to the thigh, and the hair of the masters, and extend them evenly; then cut with a sharp knife across the middle of the veins, as far as they are revealed, and then scrape from each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then take an awl or double-pronged needle, and tie it to the first limb where the blood came out, and tie it on the other side; then align them straight in the middle of the body, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted blood; then cure the wound as the others or one would bandage, so that none of the veins are torn; for by this no harm comes, and if all the veins come out, it is necessary to pull the veins from all the limbs; so that the bone does not lose its connection due to the incision of the veins, and dry and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the tooth
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this fracture are due to the section that comes out from the tooth or the extension over the belly in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from that fracture to one of the sides; and this fracture is either from the tooth or from the extension of it, and these two methods of many causes are: from the impact, or the jump, or the shout, or the lightness of a heavy blow, and similar things; and the signs when it is the extension of the tooth, it is that it has little and little, in long tension, and does not come suddenly; and it is the abscesses equal to the front, because the tooth is close to the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs of the cutting of the intestines are when it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and there are various appearances of abscesses outside the skin, and this is for the end of the intestines and the heart due to the cutting of the intestines.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are torn with the cuts, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer from the wound, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cases of iron, because it is feared that it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the way of the work is that you command or fear that the intestines be rolled up in your hand inside the wound, if it can be pulled back; then hold them between your hands and loosen the ribs; then bring the forehead above, and cover all the skin of the belly with a cloth according to what you have to open the wound; so that the white intestines do not come out through all parts; then cut off the intestines that are outside the skin of the belly, as far as the white intestines that are outside the skin of the belly and between the second intestines, and behind the belly, and between the second intestines; and move your right hand inside the belly of the belly, and hold the white intestines in your left hand above, and loosen the belly towards the tail; and command the assistant to stretch the belly upwards, and remove what is behind the skin; and if you find anything, whether it is an intestine or a white intestine that is not covered, and if you find anything, put it in the stomach outside; then take a needle or a thick thread made of twelve threads, and put it in the back part of the intestines, which is after the skin of the belly; then cover the threads with the intestines, and tie them into two parts, so that no vessel that the threads pierce can enter into wounds, that an abscess does not form; and put on the first thread according to the first thread, and after these two threads leave the part of the intestines that is outside the belly of the belly the great of a thumb; and then the other according to the roundness that the belly carries; then cover the part that is outside the skin of the belly, as we have said before; then moisten linen with oil, and put it on the wounds, and then moisten the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white pustule that we have mentioned after incision, due to fear of blood clotting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the wound remain until it heals; and if it takes too long to settle, then add hot vinegar on top of what we have mentioned, until it heals; then treat the wound with other treatments, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made as the branch that is together with the wound, in a way that you tie the veins, after the incision slightly above the opening; then cover it, and treat the abscess with what works, until the veins heal; and the cure as we have mentioned, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No fractures ever come from anger, as we have said, and it opens the wounds; and no one should expose any of the intestines to the air, and if they do, it is only for a short time; and every hour, if it remains too long in this state, the wound will swell; and this happens from the extension of the intestine which is in the fracture, as we have said, because it is stretched, then it is softened and inflated the wound and opened; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have previously said; and no cure is ever done in this way: and it is that the wounds are closed over their back between your hands, then cover the wound of the fracture with a wide cloth according to the quantity of three fingers; and then pull out the intestine which is outside the skin that encases it, then take the two ends of the intestine apparent of the fracture over the top of the belly, and press against the front of the belly, then cut the two ends of the intestine apparent of the fracture over the top of the belly, and cut both; then pull out the top of the wound, and do not cover the fracture or stretch the skin or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the ruptured intestines; then cure by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, unwind and heal the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The suture is tight, and has no appearance of breaking, and the cauterization is quiet in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the shoes
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the leather of the shoes is softened in some people, because the chariots that are inside are softened, and it can be seen; and when one wants to cure it, it is necessary to let the sore lie on its back, and cut the softened leather over the natural leather; then bring together the two edges at a seam, and if you see, first remove the excess softened leather at three or four stitches; then sew between the seams, and cure it like other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	severely
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	It is customary to speak of chastisement in our law, and for this reason I wish not to speak of it in this book; and there are only two ways: one is that the patient respond to chastisement when asked, and be cured by chastisement; and the other, because we often have to chastise some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and rabbits and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that chastisement is done in two ways: either by pulling or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by pulling, make the animal sit in a high heat, until the tendons are softened and during; then take them in your hand, until they are returned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the chastisement of the tail: it is necessary that you tie the animal, and press the skin of the scrotum with your right hand, then hang the suspensor, and cover each testicle with a cloth, when you have well burned them; and leave no drop of blood or subtle blood that is on the vessels; and this method of chastisement is more effective than that which is made by attraction, because by attraction something of the skin remains, by which the animal desires to escape. Then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodites are according to the two manners of men: one is that between the two testicles open as in the shape of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes they cut off the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another method is used in women, and it should be as high as a finger and twice as thick.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of the mouth and the anus is that you remove all the soiled rags, and treat them like other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine sprays through the skin of the anus, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tenting is a soiled rag placed on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you clean the excess of the tenting with your hand or cloths, and remove it lightly; and do not let it stay too long, as blood does not come out, then treat it like other wounds until it is healed; and another rag that grows at the mouth of the anus, and use it, and perhaps it sprays, and it is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this they called the old «cow disease».
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to apply it, as we have said about the remedy, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	The following text is a medieval medical treat
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratique refers to the nature of a woman's womb, which is not always perceived, or when the uterus is small; and it is natural by birth, or due to disease that has come, or it is caused by charm, or subtle or sharp spirits, and it is made in the marsh, or in the cost, or outside, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, and pregnancy, and possibly the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by looking at the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears nearby, it is near the shoulder or the arm.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle swelling, and it is near the two shoulders, then hurry, and do as follows: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the two shoulders, forming them until the subtle swelling is removed, and it is over the swelling; then take linen, and soak it in oil, and place it on the limb, and bandage the woman to bed each day, so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and rough, then it is necessary to use a poultice similar to a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is from a horse, if it has been exposed to the air and the cloth; and have the remedies stanching blood, such as acacia, blood of dragon, incense, abundant amount of oil; then apply a large piece of clean linen, so that the wound cannot close; and thus let it drain, and apply a tent of dry linen; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh there is a horse wound, if it needs to be covered, then do so in this manner, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is in the marsh, one should not touch with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually bleed, and when the hemorrhoids become old, they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division the similarities of these, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thrombosed veins, when they are pressed in the marsh, do not open unless they are treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that can be felt at the edge of the marsh, those are the ones that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, it is necessary to place the woman in a cold house, then pull out the thrombus with pincers, and cut off its root, then powder over medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia and sulfur and incense, and similar things; then boil her feet for an hour, then place her in very cold water; and if blood comes out, sit her in a decoction of sumac and scrapeings of green pomegranates and galls and similar things, and then take flour of wheat, and mix it with honey and egg, and make an ointment on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	If he is thirsty, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, give him suction cups to the back and breasts without injury; then take the linen, and moisten it in juice of plantain or juice of comfrey with old wine, and apply to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ready to burst, treat the wound with hot compresses until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough boil, if it should cover it as I have said the thistle; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of boils on the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of boils come in the marsh, such as chancre and pustular abscess and herpes and esthiomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and chronic abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must mention in this treatment the chronic abscess that comes in the marsh, which is not among the other types of boils; and if you know how to treat with iron, look to see if the abscess is aggravated at the beginning of its coming, and if it causes chill and fever, and if it becomes red, then you should see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce it, but make him endure the pain for as long as possible until the pain is relieved; and then place the misaligned part on a chair, and have two small chairs where he can lean, and support his back and gather his feet to the sides of the leg; and let his knees be spread out, and put his arms away from his hips, and tie them firmly with a good rope; then bring him the instrument used to open the mouth of the marsh, from which afterwards comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument being prepared, you check the depth of the marsh, so that what goes into it does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not hurt the misaligned part; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marsh with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it is necessary for him to put the horn of the instrument on top, and to stain the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and one does it by hand, if it needs to be covered at the head, with the spongy lead; and when the wound is empty, it is necessary to put moistened linen tents in rose oil or green dry oil; and place the tent from the wound to the parchment of the marrow, and place on the other side of the parchment and on the clean netted linen moistened with vinegar or malmsey, so that the wound is cooked; then cure after two hours of oil application until it is healed; and never lift the parchment and the wound by a poultice of vinegar and honey, and then vinegar or roots of lily and aristolochia are boiled; then reapply the oil.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed in marshy ground, it is necessary to be careful not to cook with iron, but cure it as we have said in the section on division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The midwife is first to the birth that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman approaching, and desiring to smell the air: then hasten the child to issue; then wipe that child according to the natural figure, and it is born with its head, and the second with him; and when you see these signs, if it is necessary to gently press her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends on its head, and the second is with him, and it is washed in the marsh of its superfluities by good cleaning; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes up from its feet, and comes forth through the back or the shoulder, and the hands, or it comes up over its belly, or sometimes, and is turned over its own collar, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the dancer that she be wise and skillful in these things, and if she goes wrong and is deceived, I will show you all the figures how one should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out of its head naturally, and the woman gives birth with great pain, and her strength is weak, then let her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and after her natural oil or fenugreek is cooked, and then give the dancer between her two little fingers the small spatula of which here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and pierce the second joint, and cover it with a bandage until the moisture that is inside has gone; and take the belly of the woman so that the infant descends, and if it does not descend, then you must cluster the woman with fenugreek musk with sesame oil; then let her inhale and spit out the condition, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if this now makes the infant descend.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are dislocated, then you must gently and gently put them back in place; and if they cannot enter, then let the woman sit on a chair, and lift her feet up; then raise the chair over the ground, and tie the woman, so that she does not fall during the raising; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cover the hands with the cloth that was previously placed on the belly, and extract the child, and put it back in place gently.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's feet above
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on its feet, if it is necessary to put it up high; then gradually turn it over and over, until it is even; then take both feet and extend them gradually.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps from the crib, if it is able to grab it, and make it sneeze with condition; if it jumps far, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, then gradually turn it over and over, until it is in accordance with the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is definitely.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have described, take muskroot and wormwood oil, melted gum, and ground in a mortar; and put on the woman's nature inside and outside this pessary, then make her sit in a high chair until above the ribs; and when she is softened, apply a mustard plaster, and remove it, and let her rest for an hour; then make her sit on a stool, then make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child is born now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the end of the child's fingers
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the infant comes in this form, place your hands gently and gently on its back; then lean it over your shoulder, and hang its legs down, and lie it on the bed; then gently fold your hands and gently press them on its stomach, and remove its clothes little by little until it is clean; and if the infant does not cry, take its feet and gently move them upwards, then gently move its stomach upwards, then push your hands down; and gradually bring the infant to the breast; and feed it gently; and command the woman to hold it until the infant is finished.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out wide a hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to engineer to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, then lift the woman, and go; if she cannot go, then make her lie on the bed, and bend her legs in a way; then remedy the muscle that I have told you about; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the chair, then study to bring back the hand; and nurse the child according to its natural shape, and make it suckle, and command her to hold it until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the issue of the child on its neck, and let his hands be spread out, and his face turned towards the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the midwife wash her hand, then turn it slowly and gently; and when it is even, if she puts on the muscle-like substance of oil and grease, as we have said, then command her to move slowly; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to breathe; and make her spit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way, for all the others
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to doing this with all the others, if the second one can hold her hand under her face and on her neck, cover her mouth so that she is not held, and the child dies; then close the child inside, as you have put it, and command the woman to breathe only once: then she will be free.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four at a time; and this is not an unusual thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is an unusual thing, and they do not live long, unless named; I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the sac that gives birth to them, which is connected to the womb; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one at a time, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born forcefully, as the cure as we have said, and if the birth canal is subtle, and do what it does quickly and lightly; and do so that it is done well for their health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Never are formed in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, or more than fifteen, and all are formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the skilled physician, and it is advisable that the midwife examines everything, because by chance similar things happen to them; so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When caring for the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and if it does not come out, and you are forced to perform a manual delivery; then it is necessary that you examine whether the woman is of sound health, and has no accident or fear of death; then it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her knees raised; and the midwife applies two fingers into the vagina if she is lying in bed so that she is not treated by the extraction of the child; then rub the mouth of the uterus with moist oils made from garlic and fenugreek and linseed, then apply the midwife's hands with these oils and these oils; then apply them lightly into the uterus, then if she swallows the instruments that are suitable for her, and if the child is apparelled that it descends over its head; then apply the instruments in her eyes or on her neck or in her mouth or in her palate or behind the beard or at the temples or near the ribs, and if the child descends over its feet, then apply it or poignil and to the sides of the middle; and it is necessary that she grease the instrument with her right hand, and place the forceps between her left hand's fingers, and press it at all her hand lightly, and apply the instrument in any of these ways that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the shape of the instrument:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find the other bone opposite, where the doctor has skill, so that the extraction is equal; then move it equally from one side to the other, to make it come out, and hold the bones in place, as follows:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, apply some of his two fingers oil, and push it into that part, and pull out the other part; and if it does not remain, put this bone or higher up, and do so until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, then you must wrap it above the wound, until it all comes out; then cover it in the joint of the foot or at the heel, and thus you must do in the other hand, and on both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	For the child, if it is large and stiff at the end, or if it has a sharp bend in the spine, you must insert the spatula between your fingers, and straighten the spine; or you can use the tool called «almidach», from which the form comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one; and thus the same is done for the child with a great natural bend; and then remove the bones with pliers, and if the child jumps up and is held at the forceps, if they are broken, cut them until the blood issues out; and if it cannot issue, then cut it piece by piece as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or outside the ribs, you must prick it until the blood flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the infant is above its feet, then the traction is light, and the pressure at the mouth of the marsh is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if the infant is stiff in the belly or the foot, it is advisable to pull it out with a rolled-up cloth over your hand; and when the belly or the foot is loose, until the moisture that is inside is removed; and if the other member is broken, and the injured one remains, then put your hand in front of the marsh, and pull it to the mouth of the marsh; then put the first or second cloth, and pull it out; and if the mouth of the marsh is retracted due to abscess that has come, it is not advisable to struggle, but it is advisable to administer moist and greasy things; and the ointments are plasters, and they are in high moistening and softening and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if it is above the shoulder, and you can put it back in place, then follow what we have said about setting a live child; and if you cannot do that, then cut off the first piece, and leave nothing of the second.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done that, then follow what we have said about treating abscesses that come in the marsh; and if blood comes out, it should be bandaged tightly, and other treatments should be followed.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had died, then consulted the other about it, and refused to let the others die.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some abscesses appeared in the armpit, and they swelled up so much that they burst, and then began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to the doctor, and I thought for a long time, and I could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong adhesive plaster, and it stuck to some bones, and after some time, it stuck to others.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound, and I saw many bones, until the woman was in much better condition; and then she had a little blood in her urine; and I do not remember this chapter except that when masters find an unusual thing, they know how to give help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	bring the marsh back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	then comes the form of pressure, with which one opens the books; and to the second returns to the second questions of the two joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the restraining device, and should be made of iron or wood; and the mouth of the fist should be two inches wide, and the margin of the trees one palm and a half; and between the two joints should be two supports of this same fist, which should be firm in both, half a palm long or a little more; and these two supports are pushed into the mouth of the marsh when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with a more subtle and lighter appearance, should be made of an ebony or boxwood rod, according to the appearance of pliers; and it should have two joints, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you want to open the jaw all the way with the instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet together and her legs spread, then push the two joints together into the jaw, and hold the head of the instrument between her teeth; then work your hand with the instrument equally, as you would with pliers, according to the amount that you want to open the mouth of the jaw, until the ball does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These tools are all mounted on top, and they have many similarities; and when the mirrors have them aligned, the work is faster, and higher for people due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not ignore the tool that you have not aligned, for its need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second instrument is held in the child's mouth, it is necessary to command the patient to hold their tongue, and then to spit out the condition, and to hold your hands on their mouth and nose; and if they cough through it, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take the pot, and make a hole or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as rue, anise, camomile, cassialigne and centoire; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled over the fire; then put a cloth or cover in the pot, and the other head in the mouth of the marsh, and let it sweat until the vapors come inside the marsh; then make him spit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second hand is also affected.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and is not completely healed, command the bailiff to have her right hand anointed with wheat oil or mussel shell, and then put it in its natural position, and find the second; and when she has found it, grasp it and stretch it gently and correctly, so that the marsh does not hinder the extraction; but move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and disappear.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the tongue of the mouth is injured, we have said the cure of expectoration and fumigation of herbs; and if she does not follow all that we have said, do not force her to vomit; but it is advisable that what is at the mouth of the tongue, you tie to the woman's cheek, then smear with the ointment tetrafarmaçon; so it will heal and be restored, and it will come out well. However, when she vomits if there comes a bad odor to the stomach and head, and causes pain.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is advisable to use the following fumigations: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cresses and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to smoke the woman during retention of flowers and secondary is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like a wire resembling a horn, and one puts the head subtly into the fire, and the smokers are wide above the fire; and let the smoking be over the charcoal, and the worm until it is tired, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not pierced the foundation, but one has stopped it with a subtle thorn: therefore it is necessary for the mother to pierce that thorn at its proper place, and not pierce too deep into the skin, and cover the wound so it does not touch it; then put on moistened linen in wine and oil, then care for the wound until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not set, place or insert a splint, and let it lie for some time, and it should be supported as the child wants to go into the chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this stoppage of pus from a wound or an abscess; if it should occur: if it is treated, as we have said of the splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula deep foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodular and thicker than those that come above the foundation or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodulation is ancient, it works, and becomes moister with white or subtle blood, and never are these fistulas persistent; and they are known by the fact that there is egestion or ventosities when the patient makes egestion, and perhaps some verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that perforate the bladder, and perforate the half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the hip, and perforate the buttock.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the basement, and not passing: and it is that you must bore your finger or basement, and insert a thin needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, if you bore a thin tent of leather, or horsehair, until you feel the tent or the hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no puncture egestion or ventositeit or ver, as we have said: saiches that it does not perforate more; then hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is perforated just above the bladder or just below the urethra, if it allows urine to pass, and cannot be cured by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated just at the junction of the thigh, then the tendon comes down to the bone; if there is no twisting and the location of the pain is not clear, then it is as if it is already healed, and there is no cure by medicine or lancing; and in these perforated fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of those who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not yet perforated and is not yet old, in hope of healing by fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the pains are hidden between your hands on its back; and it lifts its legs up to its knees, and its knees are bent towards its belly; then boil a tent of lead, or of plaster if there is twisting, until you clear out the tent.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain around the base, it is necessary that you insert your second finger, as if you are trying to feel where it has perforated; and whether it is discovered or not, between your thumb and index finger, immediately remove it; since there is no need to struggle when it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can indeed heal many things, but this is rare; and the aid that is done, it is as if one warms the cauterizing iron according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and bring all of it out through the fistula, until it reaches below the base; and do this twice or three times, until you know that those charred parts are removed, which are similar to an arrowhead; then cure the wound with a burr, until that char is gone, then cure the wound with an ointment.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is not healthy, then it cannot be made healthy; and if the tent is placed between, and does not perforate just where it should, at the base, and between the tent and the skin, there is a thick covering of char or of syfac, and you see the fistula pointing to where the covering ends; if the copper begins at the beginning of the fistula, and goes before the tent, and then the cautery after, until it reaches the top of the tent; and it will be delivered from the tent, and closed; then cleanse those char that seem like a quill of an eagle, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if it does not return, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization has two good things: it is to know, the burning of these wounds healed, and the stopping of blood and the scarring of moisture; then cure the tents that are moldy in butter or in ground-up herbs, until the wound is no longer bleeding, and when the charred wound has been placed in the wound; then cure the wound of boils soaked in hard charcoal, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healthy and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes from just above the foundation, and is away from the body, then press on your knee or foundation, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is the thread or the suture or the charcoal, where it is close to piercing, if there are no other remedies but hope and faith, by the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut just above the foundation, or if you can put tents and treat it as before; and do not move too much in front, so that you do not cover the part that holds the foundation, and bring the excretions out through the way you want; then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it after it is cut below the foundation, or by tent or other instrument appointed; then clean the charred part of the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and to hold the fistula in the part before the foundation: if there is a lighter thing to the pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way: and when you push the probe into the fistula, it is where it costs at the base of the skin above the flesh, then take a probe perforated at the top in this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And if you push the thread into it, and push the probe along the entire length of the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is lost in the margin of the base inside, then pull out the thread of that perforated one, so that you push your own or base; and bring the top of the thread together with the other two, and hold them together, and let it lie one upon the other, and do not hold it once until the thread covers these charcoals that are between the two, and heal; then treat the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then I will pierce it in all the ways that you can, unless it is too far gone.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not matter to make the bandage as soon as it is too far gone, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiculated bone that is made for the fistula is very sharp and one-sided; on the other hand, not, because we do not know how to make it as we should, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	from the emergency
