Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emergency conditions are according to two ways: either they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in the course of time they are filled with blood, and there are one or more, and they are above the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are above have little moisture, and are filled with a little sharp or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh; and the treatment of those who have within the foundation is that you command the patient to urinate in other chambers, as long as the foundations do not become full, and they open their bladder; if you hurry, and hold them with pincers, or you hold them at your fingertip, then cover their roots; and if the spicules cannot be held by their moisture, then take them to a towel, or to cotton, or from a piece of cloth; and stretch them to both sides, then cover, and powder with any hot powders that are in the cauterant; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cauterants, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed; and if the foundations cannot be released, then clean the patient's wounds with a sharp and rough cloth to remove what is at the foundation, so that it can open widely; but if the spicules become hardened, and the foundation is strong from the foundation, then the treatment is light; and it is that you hold them at your fingertip or with pincers, and cover, then treat as we have said, until they are healed, and do not require incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to mend the seam in this manner: take a thread of twisted wool, and pull it into an awl, and then draw the thread upwards and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn back the two ends of the thread away from the needle, and if they are wide; and straighten the thread firmly, then loosen the thread, and remove the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one to let out the superfluous blood; then put above the foundation a cloth moistened in rose oil or wax, and put above the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then let him lie until they are cooked, and when they are cooked, care for them with ointment and other care, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dryly and without mercy, as the lions or foundations
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	often occurs dryly and without mercy in the intestines, and due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to scratch the skin with a sharp object or your nail above, which does not let it moisten; then treat it as it should be while it is dry; and if it cannot be dried, then begin the scraping stronger than before, until it is very clean, and then scrape; then treat it as it should be while it is clean.
dou fremit	high fever
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formication is a small appearance that is twisted in the chest, and it goes up to the front; and once the froth finds it, and one feels it like the tremor of fever, and it comes into the whole body, and more so in the hands than in other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a needle of a goose feather, or a pen of a vulture very strong, and put that needle on the tremor, until the circle of the needle surrounds the tremor all around; then turn your hand to all the needle so that you cover all around the tremor, and let it out in front, and extinguish the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that the bone is broken like a rain or iron rod in this form, and it is subtlely dislocated below and raised above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, to hold the two ends together and press them. And if you see that it burns, as it is before or in the chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the bandage
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one has ever made a bandage of silver or of lead, or of melted iron or of nails; and no one has ever made such small and large instruments, according to those that they will bring.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those who are to be nursed in the care of children and those who are small and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of this poultice is small and large, if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And I have an unsatisfactory way or the belly is tied as you see, and the cloth is inside perforated; and on one side there are two holes, and on the other one; and the belly or put medicines from a beast’s bladder or parchment, and perforate all around with small holes, and between each hole I should have an inch of space, then fill in these holes with a thread of cord twisted into X or around, and gather the belly as if it is a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if the tie to the instrument before one strong thread, then poultice; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil the head of the poultice with oil or a similar substance, then press it gently; then the assistant should apply it to both hands together until it is completely visible, then remove the poultice, and relieve the pain in his legs at the same time, and if the swelling comes out as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply the poultice in the illness of diarrhea of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then restart it as long as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the blister is on the basement or abscess, then the plaster should be as thin as for a child; and this is the form of the thin plaster above where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the section on wounds; now we will tell you about the treatment of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to what they are made of, and according to the parts or wounds that are made, and from which they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by being hit with a spear, and the cut of a sword and a dagger, or a lance or a staff or an arrow, or similar things; or those that are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because its chapter will come later.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	When a simple wound comes or the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is an arrowhead or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of abscess: if you do this immediately cleanse the wound itself if there is little blood from the wound, and cleanse the opposite side; and avoid the pains of repletion of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to cleanse, let him eat soft food, and drink no wine, and do not change his drink; and put on the wound, if there is an abscess, rose oil or sterile wine; and if there is no abscess, put on the wound if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, powder that I will say a little later; and if the wound has been moved, put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large and similar to a tailor's cut, and the lips cannot be closed by stitches, then close them with sutures, as I will say in wounds of the belly, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone and can be moved but only held by a little piece, then cover it with a bandage; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat soft foods, such as tests and cooked grain, like chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you have a piece of skin or leather for a graft, and it does not touch the bone, then cover the whole with it, and pour in warm fat, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting it, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you have a piece of skin or leather for a graft, and it does not touch the bone, then cover the whole with it, and pour in warm fat, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting it, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you have a piece of skin or leather for a graft, and it does not touch the bone, then cover the whole with it, and pour in warm fat, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting it, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you have a piece of skin or leather for a graft, and it
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the light cure is used: and you should put this powder that sours as soon as the air touches it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and grind the powder finely, and fill the wound, and hold it in place until it has healed well and joined to all its skin; then bind it well, and leave it without movement, unless it swells; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one never uses chalk alone when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the air has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound has moved, immediately apply this powder; but if it is not present, use some ointments digested with honey, or flour of barley made into a thick paste with honey, until it dries out; then proceed with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then straighten it with fine needles; and I will tell you about the main fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and the main fracture, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a bone, there is no other remedy than to let the care, and not put anything restricting, for it hurts bones and draws them; and do not put anything sharp on the wound, for the substance of bones is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but rather use soft medicine, such as chalk washed in warm sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and the linen washed in warm sweet water, and other stones of this kind, and moist bandages.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then use a bandage and bind it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and bleeding heavily and full of blood, prick or cut lower down; if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, stop it, and bandage it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the jugular vein, and the conducting vessel is damaged, do not touch the neck but return it to its natural shape; then gradually restrain it, and leave it for some time, then treat the wounds with ointments until they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all if you can, and if you cannot, leave them until the wound heals, and align it; and if the wound is fresh, powder with the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if he has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat as I have described in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from arrow or sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is from an arrow or sword wound, and the wound is deep, look to see if the hairs are growing through the wound: cut them away if the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder in the first hour for the blood that it does not clot before it comes back to the heart, and stop the pain; but apply attractive ointment twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to draw out the moisture, and let it sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor will there be any trembling of the heart from elsewhere; and when you see the good dispositions, cut away that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds and other treatments, as long as they are healed; and if they cannot be healed, and work, then make incisions where there is fistula; if the treatment is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from an arrow or sword cut, and it is simple, or pierced in the front or back, then treat it as it should be; if it is large, sew it up; and if it is small, powder it, and if it has entered the bone and has broken pieces, if the wound can be closed, and if not, let the wound rot, it will ease the extraction; and for other wounds in other limbs, use judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	belly rupture
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from the large wound the intestines or the nerves of the intestines often escape, by which the incarceration of them; and the stitching is more painful, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because one can more easily put back the intestines, if they are not put back at once; because the intestines swell quickly when they feel the cold, if they are put back more slowly, and for this reason the middle wound is worse, because it is more difficult to stitch the intestines to their place as in other II And there are four ways of healing the rupture of the belly: the two common stitches are in the seam of the belly, and the stitching of the other wounds of the body and the two other stitches are common to other wounds; and therefore they are more appropriate with the stitching of the belly, and I will say one by one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines is torn, and it is easy to set, it is done by one of the two methods: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are inflated by the heat.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is hot, heat the intestines in this manner: moisten a sponge or some mild cloth only with cold water, or boil in hot sand and copper and spice, and roast the intestine until it is softened; and never do this restraining, and it is better to let it cool before using.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the swelling depart, if the internal organs are dry or high and misaligned, because by this they enter quickly; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision with the instrument used to remove worms; and the first care is to still the tail, which we should not cut without great necessity, and this is the instrument for cutting: if you cut from within outwards and not inwards, and turn out the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	When the wound is enlarged and the internal organs have fallen out, if you can put them back in place according to their natural form, it is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part of the body away from the belly, then it is necessary to place the injured part on the patient's back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part of the body away from the belly, then raise the head and the worst part higher than the other parts, and thus manage as I said for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wounds are small, apply what you have at hand to clean the entire wound with a needle or more, depending on the size of the wound, leave a space of about an inch from the edge of the wound, and then stitch the two edges together with a strong thread; and when you have sewn them together, leave a space of about an inch, and then tie them together with a double thread. Then sew the edges of the wound evenly, leaving a space of about an inch, and then tie them together as you did before. Do not place the needles too far from the edge of the skin and the flesh, so that they do not puncture the wound before the stitching. Then cover the edges of the needles with bandages or cloths to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is closed; this method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as it requires only one needle. The second method of sewing is common, and it is that you bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the flesh to a needle or a strong thread; and when you have sewn them together, remove the needle from the part where you started, in the way that one stitches with needles; and leave a space between each stitch the width of a finger. This method of sewing is suitable for wounds on the belly, which I sewed up for someone who had a wound from a knife, which was more than an inch wide, and it was cutting into the intestines by more than an inch.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been for 24 hours, and the wound was dressed with 15 days, and cured, and was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the miracle was that he thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with any ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I put clean cotton twice a day over the wound, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two main ways of sewing: take the needle, and the thread from the part in front of the skin; when it has pierced the edge on both sides, then put the head of the suture or stitch where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the other part of the part inside the skin; and the understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furrier makes the furs, and that you leave one side of the suture once, and then repeat it on the other, until the sewing is all finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which Galen properly calls, is such that anyone can do, who assembles the two parts together naturally, and applies one of the main threads to the other main thread, in a similar manner: stick an needle or main thread near, and make it pierce that part alone, and leave the two ends of the main thread; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the part forward just above, the two ends of the main thread; then make it pierce both from the part forward just above, in two other threads that are on the other side; and this is the most common way of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	People who say this word, and no one witnesses it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, or each with a thread; and one should put one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who stitch corroies; and sewn so that when the tear is in the belly, it is more painful than other tears of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is as follows: and it is that when you cut the fresh wound to its full depth, if the physician has moved it, then reset the intestine and the wound; then put on powder mixed with charcoal, and if the physician has moved it, then apply any ointment that is present, until the wound closes; then bandage it, and be sure of the sifac, and the mirach; then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then as soon as it begins to heal, apply cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no other skill in many situations where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make communication with the main members, it is necessary to apply a light bandage soaked in warm or rose oil, and place it around the wounds, and remove the swellings; and if it feels pain or putrefaction in the belly, and often happens, then you should dress it with black wine, and immediately if the putrefaction comes to the intestines; and perforate within, and scrape out what is inside, and it is lighter to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is bare, and this is because of the plants that are in it, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and its approach to the nature of nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the intestine jumps out of the wound, put it back as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned to black, then you must tie the limb that is black, so that no blood comes out, for it has veins and arteries; then cover what is between the gut, and put the two ends hanging from the part away from the wound until the extraction when the intestine dies, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the break of the bone
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is punctured, and the wound is small, if it can be restored to some men, for I saw that a man was gutted or stabbed in the belly; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and he became fistula, and inside there was egestion and ventosity; I put care according to what I could, and did not cease to subtilize until it was healthy, and the others seemed better.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewn up, I doubted that the pains were not in his belly; and there was no pain, but he remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this manner: take a sharp instrument, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the sharp instrument opens the mouth, put it above the two lips, so that it holds its mouth above; and then cover the wound, and it is held so that it cannot slip, then put the other sharp instrument in that manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and through the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the bone breaks in the intestine, and no harm comes to the wound, and it can be tied with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of the intestine that is very dirty, and then tie it to the end of this thread with a thin silk thread, then pull the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, and draw it together; and this method of stitching is no different from the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the larger intestines, there is no remedy or healing, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	all wounds or abscesses, when they close, are universally called "fistulas", and specifically when they are cut open and opened up.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its hardness and whiteness, where one does not feel pain, and is also cut like the quill of an eye; and sometimes it is clearly open, and sometimes thick; sometimes small, and sometimes enough; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no pus, is only due to one of the EIGHT causes: that is, by the smallness of the blood or flesh; or because of its malice; or because there is hard pus inside, and on the lips, that does not let new pus grow; or there is too much drainage; or the wounds are proud, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late healing, and is ejected by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of fistulas made by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to large veins, and to arteries, and to nerves, or to the face, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the costal bones, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if they come to the property of the main member, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this kind are of great harm, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come from the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you know how to treat it, take a tin of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, if the quarter; and if the fistula is twisted, take a thin tent of plaster, because the plaster plies around the twisting; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well cover it with tents, clean it out by one of the holes, for the moisture goes from one hole to another, and cleans it; then treat it properly to your power, that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and if it is in front, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the location where he feels it; and when you will know truly the location where it is, and if it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, treat according to what I have told you, and remove the faulty part and the corrupted parts that are inside; and then cure as long as it is healed, and if the fistula is deep at the right place, it is necessary to cut it open, as much as you can, then put soft tents in medicine wool, and push them up to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous part that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments of clean, whole oil, until they are healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves cause you pain or harm to your principal limbs, as we have said; and if the tooth is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, if you clean the corruption so much that it is all removed, then cure the things injured with charms until they are healed; and if they are not healed, and remain as before, cut off as much as you can: if it reveals and wants to come out as far as you can, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, cut off as much as you can; there is no other remedy than patience; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pincers, then straighten it with the appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, take them all out, leaving none behind; and if the moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear, use copper and moisture and charms, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, apply something soothing to the wound, and leave it until the bone is completely surrounded by flesh, and then the bones will be more easily set; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, wait until the corruption is completely rotted through the bone, then reopen the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption and comes to the edge of the bone; if it should be so, cover all around the corruption, and cure it until it is sound; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The young man was around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the chest, until the matter reached the leg, and it was filled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open; but the doctor by their folly opened so high that the abscess opened, and there was much matter flowing out, and became a fistula, and many more were sweating from the body and moisture from the chest; and many more doctors were consulted within two years, and there was no remedy in the art of hands, so that I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what was flowing through the pores had great heat; and the young man's chest became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I therefore took care, and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming to the bone from within; I saw that the rotten bone appeared to me, and thought there was no other corruption, except what I had seen; and I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but could not heal it; then I returned, and discovered the bone as before, and found the continued corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then removed it, and I was unable to heal the limb; but I could only cut around a palm of the bone, and treat it entirely, then I applied medicines; it became healthy and healed quickly, and did not require further treatment except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear it, and the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurs, but he was completely healed, and in the place of the bone grew a hard horn, and it was of good disposition and caused no harm nor contradiction at all, neither to the other nor to the coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take a bandage, and stretch it at the top of the bone that opens, and command him to extend it upwards; and put another thicker bandage than the first one above the bandage that is on the bone, and stretch the top, so that you can remove the rotten bandage from below, and reveal the rotten bandage above the bone where you see it should be, so that it does not corrode the bone; and put a poultice or a cloth outside the bone to cover the rotten bandage; and it should be as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the tooth is rotted and cannot be opened, and the rotting is in the middle or in one part, remove the whole tooth; then apply a cloth to the affected part, and stitch from one part to the other the corruption, and let the cloth cover the corruption for a short distance as we have said; and if the rotting is in the joint, cover the joint with the corruption, and stitch the bone or the part it contains on the other side; and if the rotting is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other way than to cover it; and if the rotting is at the tip of the hand or foot, this thing is very difficult, but nevertheless you must ask about this corrosion, how it opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not make the vein or nerve against each other; and know that the instruments for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of the teeth, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore you must prepare a tool for every kind of work, and know that the work will show you the tool that you have to use, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool that you have to use according to what it is suitable for.
dou feu	For the fire cautery
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The patients who have been bitten or stung by a poisonous creature, either by the bite itself or by the creature's fangs; and when you have medicine to treat that corrosion by the cure of medicines, and it does not help, then you must amputate that member up to the joint where the corrosion comes from, so that the poison may escape through the wound, either by death or by the greater malice, which is the lack of the member; and the signs are that the members turn black, so that it seems as if they were burned by fire, and become darker afterwards, then those corrosions of the member spread from one to another, and take hold of the whole body; if you hurry to amputate, and if the corrosion is at the head of the joint, then amputate and do not give them any space for the venom to reach their hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes from the hand, if the cloth is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the cloth is at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no other remedy but the quantity of its virtue; and thus do all that when the corrosion comes out: if it comes in the first joint, if the cloth after the other joint; and if it comes out, if the cloth covers all the wound; and if it goes up the leg, if the cloth is at the knee joint; and if it comes over the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the painful part die; and the way of the cloth or the bandage is such that you tie it above and below, and extend some bandages on one side, and some on the other, and wet the char between the two bands to the width of a span, until the bone is exposed; then the cloth or bandage, and put linen cloths on each part so that the wound does not touch the healthy skin, and it comes to other injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if blood comes out when you are working, cauterize the wound quickly, or put on some powders that stop bleeding; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a flexible bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in great pain: he had a black spot that seemed like fire burning, and that corrosion first came to his left side, taking over the whole side; and when the honorable men saw the corrosion, they covered the wound, and he was healed; and long afterwards the corrosion came to the right side of his hand, and it came to me, and I put on him things that repercuss after cleansing the body, and I could not stop the corrosions; and he thought that I would cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repercussing the matter; and he also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the virtue of the man was weak; and he despairing, returned to his land, and covered his hand, and was healed; and I have told you this only because it is necessary to do something else if one has the task.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never does an abscess form in a wound that is too narrow, and it lasts so long that it causes a great gathering of pus; then it bursts and perforates, and the pus jumps out, and the wound remains open like a wound; and the skin above is also as thin as cloth, and does not cover the bone, nor the nerve, and such diseases are called "sinus", and are not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone from the outside, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you must cut around it, and exactly when it is thin, like cloth; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the skin has hardened and the corruption is not yet fully formed, and the skin is charred, then the following remedy should be used: check if the breasts are large, and the nipples have a bad smell, then use an Egyptian remedy made as follows: take equal parts of milk, oil, and lard, and cook them together in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then add water according to your need, and make it into a poultice, either thin or thick, and apply it to the breast, and bind it tightly; leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by sprinkling; do this many times until the breasts are clean and soft; and if the pain is too great, and the Egyptian remedy and the water of ashes do not help, then use a poultice of honey and wine, where the honey has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine makes the flesh soft; and when you have done this, and you are sure that the breast is clean, then use a plaster made of frankincense and rose oil and wine; or use some other medicines and ointments, as I have described their properties and uses; and if the nipple of the breast is small, and the clister cannot enter, then enlarge it with a needle a little, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon, until it is large enough to enter; and if the wound is too large, then leave it alone until the leather or the clister can enter, and if the discharge from the breast is above, then cover it with a cloth or the lower part of the leather where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bone is broken, do not let it heal crookedly; and if you cannot cover the wound as you see fit, then arrange it in such a way that the bone heals at its lowest point where it is broken, for when the bone is broken, do not let it heal crookedly, and if you cannot cover the wound as you see fit, then arrange it in such a way: that the bone heals smoothly downwards, and leave nothing of the bone; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and lay them over the linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cover the forces at the end of the wound with a larger piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound to align the bone, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days, one time; and the one who is on the wound should often take it off to relieve the bone, and see if there is poison or little or much, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in a certain way and you see that nature has healed over the wound, then remove the bandage and approach the health; and then remove it in the morning, or the next day, and when you remove the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the poultice.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if his breast becomes full of undigested food after many hours, separate the breasts so that they do not swell.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are cut after long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who take long to heal their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if his breast becomes full of undigested food after many hours, separate the breasts so that they do not swell; and if his breasts are slow to heal and are distant, then apply moist substances in substance and dry in virtue, such as ointment definite, for there is a great part of glass, and this is the last medicine; take ointment definite, and make it with rose oil, and the same wine boiled in substance; then cook and use it; and the same thing is made with honey when it is cooked and enlarged, when there is no ointment definite present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder over the honey as it is on the fire; then apply the cloth to the breast, and use it; and never administer an aristocrat long, and roots of lily celestial, which is also like flour and hundred; and use simple or composite: grind them, and make powder, and put over the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is long and is not cured by this cure, then separate the corruption that is in front, and make impression on the bone, or on hard members, or on limbs; so the cure of the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the elbow
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the elbow due to a pouch of the hand, or a wound, or by chance in other places; and when it is opened, and no care is taken, if the abscess comes out, and corrodes and flows so much that it reaches the root of the elbow, and perhaps corrodes the entire thing; and then there are pains like those of the marrow, and the patient has a large swelling, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not improve, then you must cut off all the excess that remains of the elbow, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bones are healthy and the joint is sound; and if the joint is close to the flesh and begins to prick and swell, it is necessary that you remove the flesh that does not point to the joint, and cut off the swollen part, and apply hot and corrosive medicines on top of the remaining flesh until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, it must be cut out and removed, for as much as the bone rots, it cannot heal; and if you see that both are rotting, then cut out the rotten parts as previously mentioned, and treat until it heals; and if it is fierce, and swollen, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary to first heal the wound; then cut the joint carefully in small pieces, and make sure that the cut does not reach the flesh that is outside the joint, for the hairs would feel too much pain; and if there is, put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of a sore hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The injuries that arise in the hands of some men are all crooked, and sometimes they have bones, and sometimes they have thorns, and sometimes they have nails, and none of them arise at the root of the joint or in any of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who arise in no part of the finger do not move, and those who arise at the joint of the finger, sometimes move; the length of the crooked one is light, like this: cut it at its root with a wide saw.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who arise at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you take it with a hook.
