En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those born with or should have at the back not, it is necessary to first cut the round bone well to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable silk for this, then care until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same that comes together in both cases comes from birth, or from the healing of a wound, or from burning by fire, or from similar things.

If it is necessary to cut that which is diseased, so that the part returns according to its natural forms; then place between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, so that it does not heal; or you place between two pieces of thin leather, until the part is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When someone comes to you with either of his hands, if it is dislocated, then fix it as it should be.
des vils	of the fingers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are large and swollen, filled with excessive melancholy, which come from many members of the body; and more so in the legs of those who stand and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should never give them any purgation of bile, and then the healthy from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is according to the two methods: one is that you remove it, and draw out all the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein, and draw out all of it.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The belly is done in this way: first, the first leg of high hot mustard, so that the big one is not subtly removed, then strain the leg with the bad one below the hip; then cut the vein in the left, or II, or III, of a wide knife, then release and pull out the black blood to your hand, from one to the other, as much as the power of the bad one can bear; then tie it up, and command that he be anointed with foods infused with black coal; and then repeat the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are flat, and not painful.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the shoulder is as follows: if there is much hair on the affected leg, first shave it, then place it in hot water or bath until it turns red and the veins swell; if you don't have a bath, heat it over the fire, and then apply a warm cloth to the vein at the back of the knee or in the lower part of the thigh; then rub the skin with the palm of your hand until it appears when touched; it will appear red and black, and look like a white rope; then pull it out from the skin until it is clear of the skin, and then wrap it lightly with a bandage, then apply warm cloths to the other side for about three days; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it to the elbow, and lift it again with a bandage as you did before; then apply another dressing, or more if you have experience, then lift it, and apply warm cloths to the other side of the elbow, then pull it out and lift it to the second dressing; then remove the dressing from the wound in pieces, until it is all removed, then apply a new dressing; and if you cannot pull and lift it, insert a large needle through the thread very tightly, and pull and lift it, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it is all removed; be careful not to let it stick, for if it sticks, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it will cause harm to the wound; and when you have treated it all, place a soft cloth moistened with wine and rose oil on the wound, and keep it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the eye is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must torment it but do not cover it; and treat it as we have previously described.

de la voinne civile	of the vein civil
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is injected in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in dry land where there is no moisture; and by chance it may grow in other parts than in the legs, and if it has the pus that comes out of the skin, as it comes from within the flesh and bones, inject between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the limb changes, and the vein begins to issue, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth of one and a half to two fingers wide, and wet, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it is not too long, if you wrap it around the cloth, and wet; and if it is too long, cut a part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cover it at its root, until it is all out; for if you cover it, it will return to the vein, and bring abscess and inflammation or the limb, and bad disease; therefore it is necessary that it be treated little by little, and nothing remains or scarred; and this vein does not occur when it is treated from the palm of hand, or ten, and some have come to me, to which it issued from ten palms long, and when you cover it, it swells up or bursts, and perforates to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and let the matter that is inside be emptied, and administer medicines in the form of injections for inflammation any day, then cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never apply it to this vein again, and especially when it opens at the joint of the thumb, or the thumb itself, and there is much pain, and it falls back; then cure as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of verses that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cow disease", because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes through the entire body going up and down, and is felt in each member after another, until it reaches the skin where it went, and jumps out; and it is caused by some humors, like worms and lumbrics and ascarides or intestinal worms; and its evil is unknown, because as it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the brain, perhaps it enters, and destroys the brain; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see that the patient needs to be cured and drawn, it is necessary that you place the limb above and away from a very tightly bound bandage, then cut through and remove it, and if the blood comes out in front of the char, you do not remove it, but cauterize with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrupts the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, hold it away from it firmly, then cut through and remove it; and it is necessary to use the remedy of healing of bodies with solutions of medicines for the bad humors for the evils.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "windiness", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I will tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered one of her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the armpit of that arm; and soon after, I saw it grow as high as a worm at the shoulder, much faster than anything, just like living silver when it cuts through flesh. The pain departed from that arm, and went into the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that she turned inside out around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from one member to another, for I had never seen this disease move in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had heard that it often moved from one limb to another, but I had never seen it move in this way. I thought that it might be because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were exposed, and because of this constraint, it appeared only to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease and the pain it causes, if it appears as we have said, then place the limb above and below quickly, and then cover it with a cloth until the constraint of the venous blood is relieved; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it in your eyes, then treat the cause of the venous blood as with fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their resemblance and according to the type of animal they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of them is such that there are those with large points, and small, and barbed, and sharpened; and those with two angles, and those with tails, and those with pieces; and the one that pierces any member as follows: or in a principal member, if it pierces the brain, spine, liver, lung, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it pierces any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about later, appears: it is necessary that you attempt the extraction of this arrow, because many die afterwards in various positions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not stuck, remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the head when the arrow pierces and passes through the bone, and the syphilitic sores that are above the head, are blindness and dizziness and spasms and burning of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without strength in the nose or the ears; and perhaps also the speech and voice; and a white discharge from the wound that looks like pus, and also blood that looks like bruised char; and if these signs appear to you, then take care of the patient and remove the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of a broken rib when it breaks or pierces the chest are that it is near the right breast, and feels like it has been pierced by something hard, not soft; and perhaps the rib also moves like a chicken's wing, and there is black blood, and cold sweat, and syncope: therefore, without doubt, the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrow has not been removed is that without any pain bubbles come out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the colors change, and the patient gasps for breath and seeks the cool air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the quilt of the worst kind, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and shortness of breath; and they move all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the stomach, by chance, it may cause undigested meat to come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the belly, and it does not come out through the intestines, there is no hope of cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the bladder, and the urine comes out and flows from it, and the pain is very great: the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and back and spine and buttocks and knee and foot, and similar limbs, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow that went through his arm into the root of the nose: I tried to remove it, and took it out from the other side, outside the ear fat, and he was cured without any problem.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And to a man who had an arrow in his fat outside of the paper outside, and the arrow was replaced, and he could not reach it except with the point towards the top, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, all of it light without ears; the wound was cleaned, and no bad accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And to a Christian who had an arrow in his neck, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I cut off the barbs, and subtly removed it until I removed it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And to a man who had an arrow in his head or stomach, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, and pulled it out, and removed it, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to help a man who has an arrow sticking out or on his back, and the wound was closed over; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural positions, nor found any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to help another man who had an arrow sticking out in his face, and the wound was closed over; and it remained thus to suffer great pain; and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow to the man of the prince, the king, who had it in his neck, and was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely healed I was called for after it was three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I stretched it with a very thin tent, and I did not feel anything; and he felt no pricking or pain outside his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow; I put under his eye a mustard plaster to draw out the poison, because the eyes did not swell; and I saw the arrows in his eyes.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the plaster on for a while, and immediately healed the wound; and the hairs remained long and stretched, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed the medicine of corrosive acid on the wound with my hands, as long as it was open, and tested it, and felt the head of the arrow that was stuck in the shoulder; then I applied the corrosive acid again through the opening of the wound, until the arrow appeared visibly; and it healed well within four months, and then I extracted the arrow, and my own tools, and could not remove it; therefore, I continued to subtilize and engineer in various ways of instruments, until I got a good tool on the day after, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I removed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it nonetheless, and it was soaked in the wound, and the pain was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you might place your care on what I did not say, for the books cannot comprehend everything; but wise masters know well a few great things, and on what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not issue from members or they are not fixed firmly because according to the two methods: either by the way they enter, or by another part; and the one that has come out by the way it enters, is an arrow entering in its own flesh, and has never been removed.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her remain until the charcoal is poured around her and she is suffocated; and also if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let her remain thus for some time, and move her every day; and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, pierce all around with a subtle foret, until the bones around are expanded, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the head bone, and goes towards one of the bellies of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned cause harm to the patient: do not draw it out immediately, but leave it thus for some time, because if the arrow comes towards the face, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not lodged in the bone only, and does not come out immediately, and remains for several days without any bad accident, then use the method to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply lodged and cannot come out, then apply tar to the wound as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the body where it cannot be seen, then apply tar to the entire wound; and if you feel it, then remove it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then leave it until the wound is large enough; and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has ears attached to hold it in place, then cut off the flesh that is stuck to it with a sharp knife, and then break or pry open the ears of the arrow, until you can remove it; and be careful not to break the arrow when you remove it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, then pull the shoulder back to its place, because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding from the wound makes it difficult for you, follow the advice we gave in this chapter about its treatment; and guard against incising the nerve and vein, and use caution as you pull the arrow out, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the hairs back according to their original form when the arrow fell out, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot do it, then put them according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in a place so that one can see or feel it: cut then above, as far as the spines can take, and then extract it: if it breaks now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, round your hand and push it into the bone, until it enters the bone, then expand the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, then start extraction again until it comes out; and if the arrow is in the arrow, and you see that it is stuck, and you administer gently, if you are administering the instrument with a pointed end, so that the point of the arrow enters the end of the instrument; and then pull out, and if the arrow is caught, push the instrument in at the entering point to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, it is necessary that you cut out the entire wound where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces or sticks in the belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cut over it, if possible; and do not cut the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then clean the wound, if necessary; and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the arrows used to extract arrows is similar to an eagle's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways to do it: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of blood.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the bleeding wound is like the beak of a bird, to put at the tip of the blood, as in this way:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pins to insert and to hold is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins of common blood
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins that are commonly sought, of which there are XVI heads, that is: II ears that are after the ears, which are called the "herbech"; and the II arteries that are in II temples apparent; and II veins that are in II armor of II eyes, which are called «aspires»; and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the II ligaments that are on the collar; and the II veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called «augeherich»; and II veins that are outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are usually drained commonly are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the right side, and is called "the great vein" by the people; and the middle one is called "the basilic", and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and is called "the vein of the chest" by the people; and the basilic is on the left side, and is called "the belly vein", and is above the foscile, and is the one that is drained, which opens clearly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the earlobe and the anulaire, and it is on the right arm; and in the leg and knee there are three veins: one is outside the pouch of the right side costeit, and the second sophene which is at the elbow of the left side costeit; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is at the elbow of the other costei; and in the other leg there are three veins.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	For the shoulder joint, which is behind the ears, it helps with ancient enemas and headaches; and the quality of the saint's remedy, as I told you, and is that you remove the main pain, and rub the shoulder where the ears are on one side of the shoulder: then press the ears against a string, until the two ears appear behind the shoulder in two directions from the top: then give it to your hand, and where you feel the hair from your hand, if it is loose; then take the needle, and push it outside the ear, then lift your hand above the ear, and rub and the skin and the ear well, it should be evenly divided, and make the blood flow until you see it; then strain and tie, as long as it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The treatment of the second arteries that are in the two temples, it is to puncture them with an old needle, and soak, and stop them with a custom-made powder on those eyes; and the quality of the treatment is as I say: and it is that the hairs strangely stretch their neck, so that the two veins are clearly visible; and it feels like the fur is out of place, then sign of itching; then lift the skin over the vein in the top of your finger index, and pull the needle out, and lift the vein up, and cover, as you have done in the other two veins, and do the blood clotting according to your necessity; then remove the hairs, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then bandage it, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of its coping and removal, and beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The salve of the vein of the forehead is as valuable as the salve for cephalic diseases of the face, such as headaches, and migraine; and its quality is that the pains are strange in twisting the neck, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called «fosseur», which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the quantity you see; then release the neck from the pain, and tie the vein until it is healed, and never again work on it with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Therefore, it is not advisable that the flames be too hot or from the side, as the bone is close, and by chance, it may break the flames when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The application of the second vein that is in the two armpits helps with the eyes, and the neck, and the jaw, and the ear in the oil, and for diseases of the face; and the quality of their application is such that the pain is relieved by twisting any part, as before; then the pain, and let the application be from the side, a little long of the flame, a little wide, because there is no harm.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is too thin, it might break; then correct the blood, as much as you have skill, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein of the nose is good for ague, and for fevers, and for facial diseases such as migraines and redness that comes in the face, and always when it is old; and the quality of the vein is that the pains tighten their neck, then straighten their nose with your right hand, and take the thin flame long, and put it on the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well, and the blood will start to flow; and do not move too much forward, and bandage the wound according to your need, then leave it for one night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the second ginger helps to narrow the alainne, and at the beginning of the melting, and with many diseases, and with pustules, and with corrosions, and with herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the salve is that the pain moves away from one and the other, as we have said; and so the masters are above the chief of the pain, and the pain sits on one seat, then clean the wound with a long brush gently, then draw out the blood temperamentally, or as much as the matter requires; then do the other side in the other wound, then release the limb, and hold the wounds steadily, so that the pain does not entangle; and leave it at dawn, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the livers above the teeth helps in chewing food, and prevents tooth decay, and cracks in the lips, and dry throat and inside.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of this health is to make the pain disappear before you, and hold its neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: compare both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, compare the largest of each part, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the tongue's disorder
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The disorder of the veins that are dislocated from the tongue is helped after the disorder of the cephalic, and it is by tightening the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the healer is that the sickness stops between your hands before the sun, and the leaver the tongue, and looks from each side one black vein: thus it is healthy on both sides, and does not move too much, for beyond are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly cured are cured in two ways: either by pinching with all the flame mirrored wide, or by a thin knife as if cutting trenches, and is called "aneth"; and they are wide and thin according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fire cautery is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has a profession to open the veins that are deeply punctured with large blood clots and disturbed; and this is the form of the fire cautery.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more finely pointed, and is for cleaning the veins that are finely punctured, where there is fine blood clots.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein cleansing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and in the collarbone, and in the shoulder, and in the abdomen; and it is necessary for the cleaner to clean well, and to be careful not to cut the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, then it is necessary to cool it, as I have said; and do not prick the flame, but cut it as with a needle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the abscess does not open clearly, then it is necessary to pierce and change another one; or you want any rain of it, or you squeeze in the vein instead of the arm: it opens clearly; and cut with a needle as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know the vein of the sainie, then it is necessary to stretch the arm until you touch the vein; then sign the vein with a needle, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a needle; and beware that you do not pierce the artery when you see the vein swell, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding high as the urine of a child, and the stain is red and thin, it is from an artery: hurry then, and put your hand longwise, then remove your hand without stopping, which has happened many times; hold the arm still, and let the hairs not move until it is healed; and be afraid, and do not move it until it is safe.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not stopped, and it bleeds, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head of the blood will retreat; and stop the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a splinter of figwood, and grind it, and take one half and lay it across the other side; if it does not stain, it is good; if it does, then cure it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the stops do not last in many positions for the small wound of the sore, and the position of the little arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The cleaning of the vein in the middle helps it treat blood from the top and the body, because it is composed of basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and the cleaner should wash all the nerves that are outside, and if he does not do so too much, and he finds the nerve, and he inflates it and the wound is healed, and perhaps it cannot be healed; and this nerve opens often, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you should clean the wound with the instrument anesthetic; and shield the nerve from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has veins between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head, and helps with the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed in pinching the olive oil or myrtle leaf, for it is the safest of all veins, because it has no nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter vein, and do not harm anything if you have to do it the first time, and start again; and by chance, some people's veins swell, but it does not matter the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about health is that health is maintained only to maintain health and to prevent diseases from coming; and it should be done in one of the three ways that are either costly: namely, cephalic, fasting, and basilic; and if you must heal at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after the sign of repletion appears; and if you must heal on the first day or third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The healing that is administered to diseases has no determined time, but rather depends on the need of the day or night, in every hour and all ten; and it does not necessarily heal children under fourteen years, nor a pregnant woman except during the first four months after conception.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They should not be treated by a young doctor who has passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When one wishes to be healed in any way whatsoever, it is necessary that they first cleanse the intestines of a light clyster if they have much feces retained, so that the veins do not draw harmful superfluities into the principal members; and they should not be healed by one who is too healthy from meats, or who is pale, to such an extent that they are hydropathic; and if one wishes to be healed after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, and abdominal pain, and frequently traveling, nursing, and fasting, and all the virtues, or by some means of the arm or body; then subtly draw out the humors, if they are not too thick, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have them; then bathe or wash, if nothing prevents, to subtilize the blood, and heal from the vein during the third hour, as we have said; and guard against that day of work, and pain, and luxury, and similar things; and be linked and joined, and let the healer be higher than those who are healed, and let him rub his hand twice or three times, then gently move the joint above the middle, for when it is too stiff or weak, it cannot be corrected; then rub the healer's hand on the wound until the veins swell, and feel the pain; then moisten the healer's flame with a little old oil, then put his right hand on top of the wound of the hand where he wishes to heal, that the vein does not fail to strike.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as quickly as strings to the barber, and some that are plain from their softness, so that when one puts above the flame, they withdraw from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus are those; and if it opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, because it is necessary that the barber be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, then restart a little from that place or above hastily, if the veins are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are swollen, and the pain spreads, leave it for an hour or two, and do not bind the arm: perhaps an abscess will come; do not enter water, then restart the lancing if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, or the stone is cut subtly and you doubt that there is as much blood as you saw, then apply the flame directly to that wound; and work a little hastily, as long as the veins are swollen; for this happens often, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the joint swells, do not start again with the same bandage, and put some oil on it, because it reduces the flow of blood in this joint, and it is beneficial for this joint like oil; and thus administer the oil in each bandage that you bandage the wounds, to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing applies to triangular and oblong bandages, when you put them on the joint; and gently apply the bandage as it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there come some large abscesses that often occur, exactly when the opening of the wound is small, you must hurry and put on the limb a soft sponge soaked in hot water and a little linen cloth, and hold it for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the flow of blood from the wound, and if it remains on the limb for several days without any sign of blackness or greenish color, then you must not remove it; and if you see anything of aloes or of myrrh mixed in some juice of calamint, myrtle, or similar thing.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often has an abscess and appearance of the saint's basilica: place your hand on it, and if you press the limb too much by the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not place anything on it that we have said, for by chance you may cut the artery; but apply a dry plaster to harden the limb, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And apply each bloodletting according to the amount of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is appropriate for one who is plump and strong, and has the task of extracting arrows, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and let them rest often and little, and let the wound be sown by cutting across, not by pinching; and this method of stitching is safe from the discharge of poison and the compression of nerves, and is better than stitching long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body is weak at the time of stitching, it is appropriate to give them bread moistened in juice of green pomegranates; if they are hot-blooded, take out the arrow three or four times; and if they are cold-blooded, change the bread moistened in honey syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and strong-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he pounds the wound after much bleeding, then it is necessary to give him a broth of bone and an aromatic syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to lance another arm, and bleed again, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleeds a little and little, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to lance another arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong pain, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And those who wish to heal on the other side, they must heal in the second hour or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has much blood within the body which is already heated, and causes fever; so it must draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein until it cuts into the flesh; then one must restore all the conditions of healing, and place one's hand upon the pulse when it begins to heal, that the patient does not die in the absence of pulse, and this has often happened, when the healer is negligent; and it does not matter if you see the arm begin to swell, and draw out blood the second time, and the vein is closed, that you press firmly upon; but if it is curved, extend the arm vigorously, for this would be bad; but let it remain as it heals the second time; or you are not at the tip of the flame, until the blood that is frozen in the vein has been drawn out, and put a little piece of cloth in boiling water, and press upon it firmly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the wound is open, leave it and do not press on it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If it is necessary to draw blood again the second time, if the healthy vein is in the same limb, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthy because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The method of vein puncture is that the hairs on the hand are burned with hot, sharp instruments until they turn red; then it is gently moved so that the vein appears well, then pricked from the side, not too wide or long; and the punctures should be wide, and the vein should be pricked close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be done, leave the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow out into the hot water until you have enough; and if it is in the arm, do not repeat the puncture in hot water, because it will cause more harm than good; and the vein puncture of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve of the hand from the right side is good for all diseases of the liver, and it is thus: strain the hand, and boil in hot water until the vein is emptied, if one sees it; and if the salve is against, and if you apply it with everything together, it does not hurt anything; and do not move too much immediately, for the nerves are all denuded of flesh, and then put the hand in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary, put oil and thread on the wound to sew quickly, and thus do for each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The left hand sweat is valuable for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you to the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sweat of the sophene is valuable for all diseases that are not in the body, such as marsh fevers, retention of flushes, and diseases of the gout, and the joints and legs of old age, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its sweat is that the diseases are driven out in high heat, and rubbed on the vein until it perishes, and tied above the joint; and the vein is at the knee, and from above the knee, they go very much to the gout; therefore, sweat is more valuable at the knee, or at the joint, than it is.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you are healthy above the knee, and there are nerves that are dislocated, and the healthy one crosses as in knitting; and let the flames be close.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot issue from the knee, reset the knee in a high position, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the healthy one needs to be done first, then start the second one a little higher, because the veins are salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so make the other knee equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the knee of the thigh, and its healthy one is equal to the pain of the hip, when it is for an arrow.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its saintliness is such that the hairs between or in bathing, and is strange above the ankle four times twisted, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is better that you cover it, for the legs are sound, and it is very often reopened by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not straighten it, then it heals none of those who open or close the small pore, and towards the little finger, and warns against the nerves; and correct as much blood as you see, and then release the ligament, and put it on cotton and hold it steady; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of wounds of suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction wounds are made of horns, or of iron, or of glass; and ventosation is done in two ways: either by puncturing and drawing blood, or without puncturing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without puncturing is done in two ways: either all at once or without heat; and suction that is done by puncturing and drawing blood is done in twelve places on the body, of which one is completely on the top of the head; and the others are under the collarbone; and the other two are on the sides of the collarbone; and the suction outside the mouth; and the suction on the shoulders; and the suction on the heels; and the suction on the knees; and the suction on the ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the body, and therefore does not weaken anyone, as is done with a bleeding wound; and it should not be administered, neither at all heat nor without heat, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessity of illnesses requires venesection, or by custom, let us perform it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in each season; for there are some who, when they have need of venesection, have heavy chests; and some who feel repletion and heaviness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck; and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and extend their tongue, and suck blood; and there are some who dream, and see through blood and nails and death and similar things.
