Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is during the month, we command them to vomit after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sweating of the head helps to relieve the pain of the head … that comes from them, and it should only be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this vomiting is in the place of the sweating of the cephalic, and it should not be used by those who are of cold complexion, or who have diarrhea, because this does much harm; and for this reason it should not be used by those who are guards, or who have head colds.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often become faint, should have the cupping glass placed a little lower due to the uncertainty of fainting.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The cupping glass is placed on the neck instead of the chest and back, and it is good for narrowing the arteries, and piercing the main channel, and to all, and for replenishment; and it should not be held too tightly, as it may cause fainting or stomach pain and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The cupping glass on the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, and obtundedness, and dizziness, and choking, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the chest treatment; and it should be commanded to the sick person to press his hand when placing it, that he does not compress the artery, and does not cause blood to flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Breathing through the nose is beneficial for mouth diseases, and decay of teeth, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Breathing through the shoulders is beneficial for diseases that come from heat and filling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Breathing through the elbows is as beneficial as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and commands the healer that he does not prick too much in front, for the inside is without flesh, and knows how to draw out nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the back should be used for emoroidal diseases from the foundation, and for diseases that are out of place, and it should be a large, metal suction cup that can properly draw; and perhaps, if it is too thin, it will break; and then great wounds are made.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg suction cups should be used openly, for they draw blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains of the rain, and of the marsh, and of the bladder, and remove the flowers; and they are in the place of the two knees, and everywhere they weaken the body after long use, and cause pain in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the vacuum is that you first apply it empty and quickly suck, then press hard and move evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the limb red and swollen, and open the vein; then stop, and replace the vacuums, and take care of the wounds, for there are some who have bad blood and clear pores: it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a few deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thinly cut through the thick blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the joint is very out of place, it must be struck a third time; and when we want to pull out the arrow slowly and slowly, we should only strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, we should often strike; and if the joint is not out of place, we should strike in front, and the end should be that the cut should pierce deeply, and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and are tough, and who have sharp nails, that you use the points of oil-soaked vacuums: if it is in summer, with violet oil or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, with pennyroyal, lily, camomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of tamarisk, or balm, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if that person to whom one wants to apply a wide and loose bandage, then one should not put any oil on it, but it should be washed after the ventilation of hot rose water, or cold rose water, or marjoram water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise with ash water, or rose water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive superfluities rise from old wine, or vinegar of soot, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and should not be made to sweat too much before the bath, nor in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and should not sleep immediately after pustulation, and it is good that they warm themselves, when they should be pustulated and when they are pustulated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are sweated are feverish, and if they are not too agitated and inflamed; then it is good that they take cold things, such as large green apples and endives and leeks at the sauce, and similar things; and they should drink milk of almonds, and char of Castile, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold constitution should take honey syrup, and aromatic wine between old and new, and a little juice, and little pinch of pepper and small birds; and the day they are about to vomit, they should drink more than usual; and it is appropriate to give some men once triphala or muscat before vomiting, or after, to strengthen the main members; and the subtle ones should not drink it, but only those who are chaste.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed on the body to cause pain are those that are placed on the liver, and in the groin, and in the gout, and on the stomach and the buttocks and the legs and the waist, because these members do not suffer much from pain on the outside, and no one does it except to draw blood from member to member, as we place suction cups on the breasts when the newborn is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the stomach and on the buttocks to soften the member; and remove the pain, when there is an abscess or a stone, if by its attractive power it happens to remove the abscess, or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it is done as long as one places it on the liver and in the groin when there is retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty for drainage only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes with a hot iron, if there is high fever, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot water, or with water where herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction applied by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two inches wide and half a palm in length, and should have a small hole in the middle, as to put an needle, and it should be of tin or lead before it is put on the limb so that it does not burn the hair when placed on the limb; and it should have a cross-shaped rod of tin or iron in the middle to place a cotton pad, and they should be large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the suctions of children are different from those of adults, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus place this suction cup on the limb: take the wax or liniment, and put it inside the suction cup at the cross of the stick that is inside the suction cup, so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup that it does not burn the hair; and then put it on the limb, and one should be above the punctures that we have said, so that when one wants, if the vapor goes, and one removes the suction cup; and take the liniment as before, and start again often, if you have need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	Therefore, in the suction cup that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, at all acute, there is no stick or puncture, and it is not administered except when it is full of acute, and it is placed on the limb alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Sansues are not applied except in members where one cannot place suction for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in those remove the clothing, such as two or nose, and others similar; and the quality of the use is that when you trueve sansues that are in fresh waters without pressure, take them; and put them in fresh water, until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then cleanse with blood and suction, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the sansues; and when they are plain, and dry, if it is a place where one can place suction, place it, for this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, first lift the limb from below, and then from above, very well, and then wipe it; and if the wound is too large after the course of the sinews, then moisten a linen cloth with cold water, and place it on top, until the wound is stopped up; and if the wound multiplies, then place vitriol or galls on it, or similar things, until it is stopped up; or you put half of pounded cloves on the wound, and leave them on until they dry on the limb, which will stop it now; and if you have more trouble, take other sinews.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the worms do not want to take, rub the flesh of blood fresh, or you have stuck a needle so that the worms in it, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will fall; and when you see that they are dying, powder with a little aloe and beaten silk, or ash, if they will now cherish.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Listen, dear child, that the folly of men has often caused this chapter to be lost, neither have they seen any of the old books nor have they read them; and for this reason the science is unknown in our land, for I found none good; and I know nothing, except by the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated it, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that will be used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we say or prologue of this book the summaries of the language and the chapters where the wise place their understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced may find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or wound comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to clean the wound on both sides, if nothing prevents, such as weakness of body, or children, or old people; or if their condition is not very cold, or too hot; and change cold damps, and chicken broth and goosebroth, and do not drink wine, and change no heavy foods, and do not fill oneself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of an abscess, or of spreading of matter to the member; if the wound returns to its former government as it has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the wound be cleaned with a thick bread dough, or with viscosity, as cooked wheat, and rice, and tests, and pie, and chicken pancakes, and eggs, and fish, and thick wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the cleaning process may cause pain and more quickly break the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken in the old and infirm cannot be properly mended or soldered according to their nature due to the age of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but rather, put them above the broken bone with large strong ones that support and join the member together, as much as it can enforce, until it enforces as it was before; and do not leave any part of its work, and for this reason, it is necessary to clean with thick foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And there are various ways to break bones in many different manners.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the breaking of the shoulder is different from the breaking of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is breaking that goes like an arrow, and another in soaking, like the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is breaking with a wound, and breaking all in a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own mechanism, and its proper tool in the restoration, according to what the memory comes in its place; and the breaking of the bone is known by the bone being twisted, and open well by defense, and it is to the pressing of the hand; and when there is no twisting nor to the touch, and the pains are not great, if there is no breaking; but it can have twisting, or cut, or small breaking.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it by hand, but apply the remedies that come after, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And if the fracture is in the arm, and the two parts are disjointed, you should now set them evenly, as soon as pus comes out; and if pus hardens and comes, do not let any pus remain until the pus is calmed; then put it evenly to the muscles that you can lightly and safely move, and if the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of that where there are pieces, then hold it as it should be afterward.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if it is in a broken bone, if it is of two parts, whether by hand or foot, or to your hand if it is small members, or to two strings, or to one string and to your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you should gradually add them back in their places with care that through your work no further injury or pain comes; and well set the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if it feels well, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring it through their work with an abscess and contraction of the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in place, well punish the bad pain that it does not move, whether awake or sleeping, turning or in any other way; and keep well that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and you should put it in the right position so that it feels no pain; and guard that it is put correctly, for twisting does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the member broken is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The broken members are different in size, greatness, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: if they are thin, cover them with soft linen cloths; and those that are thick, such as ribs and legs: if they are thick, cover them with a wide and strong cloth, for the wide cloths embrace the whole member, and strain it evenly from all parts, so that there is no gap; then wrap light bandages around it, three or four times according to the length of the member, and hold your hand a little on each side of the cloth, then go above the fracture and strain it less, than the fracture slowly remove the fracture; then soften the cloth little by little, until you grasp a large part of the sound flesh, then take another cloth and return around the broken bone; then return to the part away from the fracture, and strain it evenly, neither too hard nor too painfully, as we have said in the first chapter above; then place between the cloths a linen or cloth bandage, as much as they are even, then tie all from above with a bandage, and put your well-made bandages on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or swelling, put something soothing on the abscess and what removes the swelling, and leave it like this for some time; then strain it through these filters, and be of half a wide cloth safely, or from which the clips are made, or from palm branches, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the filter that one puts over the wound be slightly larger and wider than the others; and also as long as the limb of smallness or greatness requires; then strain through these filters just as you did in the first layer, then tie up above a thread evenly, as in the first layer over the broken part; the tighter it is, the less; and it should be that the threads are medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and of fine linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of those who make their own cords of linen thread twisted, and this is great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too delicate, and it should only have a little more than two spaces between each filter.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the hairs are torn out by the pricks of the needles after they have been sterilized, put some ointment or lint on them so that they do not become infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the stitches are broken, I will tell you the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And do not strain all the broken limbs with needles on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the limbs are large, you should not put needles in them for at least five or seven days, depending on your risk of abscess; and here is the method of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take some flour that is kept in a bag next to the mill, and mix it with an abundance of water, and make this paste, not too thin or too thick, and apply it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring fracture at many positions, and especially for women and small children, because it is not too hard or too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for healing fractures, dislocations, and twists: take alabaster, ladani, enule, and asafetida, each X amount; myrrh and aloes, each V amount; alechil VIII amount; and make a powder, mix it with honey; if the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and it quickly heals broken bones, and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster for twists: take mugat and vismalve, each X amount; myrrh and aloes, each VIII amount; bolic armenic VI amount; grind it well and mix it with vinegar or honey, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method to treat joints and bones that are dislocated or broken, to relieve pain, and to use the bone and the fracture: take a new bandage, dip it in hot oil, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These bandages do not heal, but they are good for relieving abscesses and properly treating pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method to treat broken bones that heals: take dried fig leaves and earth petrified wood, grind them together, and make a bandage.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method to treat the healing of bone fractures and to alleviate the remaining pain from the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of valerian, chamomile flowers, violet flowers, flour of each one in equal parts; and grind, and make into a paste with wine, and if the limb is cold, apply the paste with moist coriander juice or vinegar.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to treat more than the first, when an abscess is resistant to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of valerian and linseed, balm, melilot, and violet flowers and chamomile, of each one in equal parts; and grind, and make into a paste with salty water, sweet water, or wine, depending on the temperature of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb that which is made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to restore it, dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat injury and pain: take the marrow and hooves of men who have died, or feathers of owls, and vinegar, and linen evenly, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen the bandage a little afterwards, and be careful if the hairs do not feel any pain, nor have moved the bones of the limb; then do not loosen the bandage by hand again. And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, without rest or inflammation, then hurry, and loosen the bandage, and take a light cloth, and moist sponge from sea water, and plunge in hot, and raise the limb, until the itching ceases, and soothe the pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened with hot oil or rosewater, and bind it with a nut, until you are sure of no abscess forming; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and soothe the pain, then begin the thin bandage again, and a little of the plaster, and do not strain it as tightly as before; and gradually as it becomes healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess has pus and is red, swollen, and painful, and you have skill in applying poultices and bandages, if it restarts, as you did before, evenly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb as we have said within three days or four or five or seven; and never leaves it for twenty days, as long as the breaker is aware, and approaches the joint above; then it should be restrained more than before, and it will increase its flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the limb becomes too dry, there cannot be any new growth; then apply hot water frequently, every hour, and loosen the bandage a little; by this method, then, the new growth is prevented in the limb, and it is healed quickly as they do with the foolish people, who restore the limb painfully: this is bad, and if it is a difficult case, and I see nothing else but the weakening and the correct work.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various breaking ways
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many breaking ways are, and diverse figures, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks that are made of percussion of sword, and the collar bone completely breaks the bone just below it which is outside the bone, as it does hunchback or broken; and for this reason this type of break is called «hunchback break».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone from above through the point, and this type of break is called «absolute break»; and it is the wound of these two breaks great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion embedded, or cut or of fall from rock, or of falling on stone, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if he has a fracture, which approaches the tendon that is outside the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is set into the bone as delicately as a hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason it is called "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by being struck by an arrow, or falling, or something similar, and the piece of the bone enters below, and the threads are like those of a cauldron when they are pierced with a fire.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are more who have or chief moist bones, such as the head of a child; and they have all these kinds of fractures where small pieces are displaced as these; and I will speak to you about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the displacement above them, and by the inquiry with probes, and by the rottenness that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is known because when one has exposed the bone, and one rubs it above, if there is an open fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be careful of the bad accident, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes issuing forth and reddening, and other similar things in many dispositions, it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any visible injury, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the broken bone comes first to you, and it is in the leg, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the most that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the arm, then you should remove the bone before the seventh day, provided that the skin around the bone is not rotten, and the injuries we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fractured bone comes close to the skin that covers the skull, then you should remove the damaged part as follows: and you should press the head of the painful wound, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and above the shape of the wound more softly than you can, and if blood comes out when removing the bone, or an abscess forms, help it according to what is necessary, and it is that you fill the wound with moistened linen cloths in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is soothed, and make sure that blood does not come out; then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut tightly in front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then use another larger incision than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And in the second manner, you should have various incisions of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they should be sharp and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the tooth is very hard and outside, it is necessary that you perforate around it, as well as administering incisions with trephines, not piercing beyond the test bone, and it should have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you should have several of them, so that each time comes in its place on the surface of the bone, so that you have trephines for all tests; and this is the form of the three ways of trephining:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	To perforate the bone around the broken one is that you put a sharp object on the bone, and turn to your right until you know that the bone is perforated; then remove the sharp object in another part slightly afterwards, and so do all around, then cover the incisions the space of the bone between the teeth, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you remove the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools that you have such as forceps, pliers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the tongue.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perforated and treated the bone, it is advisable to close the opening of the bone to all other tools resembling an incisor, but it must be more slender and more subtle than the other incisor; and if nothing remains of the small bones, or scales, then gently remove them with the tools; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is as the Galians say, which is more safe; and it is very good, and that is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have uncovered that part, then remove the lens-shaped piece from the shape of this incision, because of which:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the broken piece is in two parts, so that the cutter is towards the bone; then use a small hammer on top, so that you lightly tap the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is outside; if it is against the bone, then lightly tap the bone, because one taps the bone too hard, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone's fracture does not pierce through the cloth, and the bone is crushed only from above, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to remove those roughnesses, and to scrape off the scales with the subtle razor that you should have various quantities of, in order to treat each limb as conveniently as possible, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you must use large razors first, and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and fracture subtle instruments, it is necessary to treat according to its advantage; and this is a matter that is not immediately apparent to him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is exposed, it is necessary to apply a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, moisten it with rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; do this more gently than you can, so as not to aggravate the wound, then administer by pouring lentil powder, flour of wheat, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it over the wound, and administer liquid medicines without causing pain; keep the wound clean, do not leave any tinder, because when tinder gathers on the brain's surface, it causes the brain to rot and suffer great harm; for when something sharp is placed over the wound, it does not heal.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, for if no accidents come to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful with doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no other remedy than the one you have placed on, which has virtue, then you must take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one cloth, and put it on the wound; then cure it with methods of cures that are appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Be careful that the two parts of the bone above are never broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and that one is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, you must bore a small hole or puncture into the nerve, and place the broken part inside your index finger, and in the palm by default, until the nerve regains its natural shape; do this lightly, and guard that the pain does not feel through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nerve, and cannot reach the finger, then you must place it at the top of a small bone.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in both parts, then make another one, and hurry to restore the first joint, if you can; if not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the swelling of the wound is calmed, then bore a hole at the top of the nerve with linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you turn the other way, if the fracture is there; and if the tents are so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said no one should clean the tents in the morning, and every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but they should be cleaned with a mixture of honey and powdered milk; then leave the tent until the bones are healed, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never use goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is a soft cloth around, and if the fracture is present, and blows the bad air away; then do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	If an abscess comes to the nose while you are working, put cotton or a piece of bread soaked in rose oil or a drop of ichthyol on it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess does not come to the nose, put a paste made of mustard flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk on it, then place light cloths over it and do not bind it tightly; if the broken piece of the nose is small and in many pieces, use suitable instruments to remove them, then cut away the wound, and care for other injured parts as appropriate, and apply suitable ointments and remedies as needed; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents and place cotton in it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured without any wound, and the fracture is not completely separated, and it is not broken into two pieces, but rather cracked inside, if one knows this clearly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, then you should press your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left side, then press your index finger with your right hand, and gently press the fracture inside, and hold it with the other hand by default, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is in two pieces, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth avails, or breaks, then strain one thread of gold or silver or silk, then place it over the broken jawbone, and place a double cloth on top; and place on the cloth a great well-made stick, or a piece of leather even in length and width according to the jaw, and tie it to the muzzle so that you can, and command the patient to rest, and feed him light meals.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, let the patient rest for a day, and then put it back in place; and apply an ointment on top, of flour from the mill with abundance of egg or flour of mustard, after you have removed the crust; and apply the ointment again, and if the disposition does not change, let it be as long as it becomes healthy; often it becomes healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes to the head, follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, cover the unbroken piece of the bone that is healed; and subtly from the healing apply it with convenient instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, then expand it as needed by fire.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is no longer any delay, if the wound is wide, put on top of it some suitable plasters, to apply charcoal, until it is healed.
de la forcele	from the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The shoulder blade is broken several times in front and behind, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and displaced into two, and there are pieces, and it is the least heavy to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And when the fracture is on the side of the wound, you should have two assistants, one to hold the injured part where the bone is broken; and the other to extend the collar towards the affected part; then set the fracture with your hands, so that it forms as it should, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round, rounded piece of cloth or linen, as large as needed, under the shoulder bone; and extend and lift the broken bone, holding the sphere in your hand, so that you can set the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you cannot pull the shoulder out of its socket by force, because it comes out in front, then it is necessary to let the hairs lie evenly on their own, and place the shoulder bone on the shoulder blade, and push the ministers the shoulder down, until the bones of the shoulder are raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then bring the fracture to your own, and if the fragments are broken, it is necessary to saw them; and carefully remove the pieces, and if the bones cannot be joined for any reason, then use one of the instruments you have; but put the tool away from the shoulder to prevent infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It resembles a spoon, and is not straight, and should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the workman; and have two prongs, like this, and one wide and the other narrow, like the edge of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of an abscess, if you cut the wound, and if the edge is small, or you doubt an abscess, use the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, if you moisten the cloth with rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	For the fracture of bone, whether it is near the skin or deep inside, you should place a plaster of powder from the mill and some flour on top of the bone, and put light bandages over it, and place a sphere outside the joint if you have skill; then take a very large bandage of about a palm's width, and double the cloth over the bandage and the plaster; then take a thin strip of cloth about three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the larger bandage, so that the head of the larger bandage hangs down; place the thin strip on the fracture, and roll the larger bandage up from the collarbone to the shoulder, and remove the sphere outside the joint, and remove the badly aligned part; then align each part, and if you see that the patient tolerates the thin strip evenly, and clearly see that the thin strip does not move over the broken bone, reward every day, and when the limb is free of pain, restrain it; place the badly aligned part on its back, and put a small piece of cloth outside the joint as a support to lift the fracture up; align the break by aligning the shoulder, or tie the arm to the collarbone, and do not move it unless there is a bad accident in the next 20 days; then begin again with the plaster if you see that it is necessary, and tighten and leave it until it is healed; it is healed in about 28 days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	There are few cases where the shoulder breaks or moves out of place, and it is not fixed except by touch; if the splint according to the figure of the fracture, and the shoulder is put back in its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on the bone powder from the mill with abundant water, and light dressings, and put a double cloth; then put on a wide and delicate splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is not in any part of the shoulder, use the hair of the bandage so that the splint is evenly; and then tighten it all with a strong bend, so that the splint does not move from its place, and watch it every day; and every time it breaks, tighten again, and if it is far from its place, and ease the pain on its side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25. And when these numbers are completed, remove it, and be careful, for this is not bone that is put back firmly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is torn off before, and not removed from the wound, then cut through it, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the finger to relieve an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the pinky
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The little finger is never broken in the middle, but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines outwards, and the patient feels great pain, and the finger is crooked, and everything, and perhaps blood flows, and the bones are exposed in the broken bone, and the smell is bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the hairs are arranged evenly on top of their backs, and the handkerchief is placed between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades, and gather the ribs of the two ribcages in your hands, and subtly put them in place in all the ways you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then place bandages and poultices above the thin bone of salt, or another light one, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so it does not move; and return the limb gently to the back, and gradually tighten it, and reward every hour with the book, and if it moves, tighten it; and if it is necessary to release it for corrosion or for itching that comes to the skin, or pain or abscess, then hurry and release it, and replace the bandage, and address what has come from methods of treatment; then reapply the bandage, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The fracturer of the ribs comes only from heavy blows to the chest and the back, and the head inside, and they do not come unless because they are sharp; and one feels it well at the inquiry as we have seen.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the poultice, and the bandage of a splint, if you have skill in that.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inward, it feels great pain and sharpness, like pleurisy, because the bones do not pierce the skin; and they must be lanced, and everything must be drained of much blood, and this is a grievous sickness, and the ancients have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if among those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the stomach, to push the rib outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We should not do this, unless there is an abscess present.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then the healthy one.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that none of us should put suction on the limb, for it is good for draining, and this seems to be reasonable; however, there is doubt as to whether the suction will draw the excess from the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that none of us should cover the limb with soft cloth in hot oil, and then put tents between the ribs to keep the lung even inside, then treat the care of pleurisy, food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pain is great that they cannot bear it through the bone that does not cover it, and there is doubt, then you must cut across the broken rib on the side, and you must place an instrument to keep the wound open; and then you must saw the bone, and gently pull it out, and then stitch the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat them with ointments, until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.
