And if an abscess comes on the skin, then place moist cloths soaked in rose oil on it; and treat it while the skin is healing from the abscess, and let it lie down beside it where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck bone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes when the breaker breaks the neck bones, and often it does not rain; and so on the backbone.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know whether it will be healed or not, if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or extend them, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	It is said that it is deadly in many positions, and if they move and feel well when held and not, then it is said that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the pains are healed, if one puts on care.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing comes to the spine in the back, and you know whether it is healthy or not, if you notice if the feet are soft, and if the accidents that are in their hands, and above the back suddenly ventilates and egests without volition; and when it is laid on its belly, if it suddenly egests without volition.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is laid on its back and it wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal: do not attempt to treat it.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to it, then the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the care is that you reward if there is an abscess open, to put on the back rose oil or chicken fat, as long as it is calmed; then put on one of the healing plasters and drying, and tie with a bandage, and command the pain to rest; and do not sleep on that part where it hurts, as long as it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dry, it is necessary to cover with the cloth; then remove the bone, then assemble the two flaps of the wound, if it is large, at a seam, then cure the ointment applying char, as long as it is healed; and if the bone is broken, which is called the «broken bone», if you have a pouch in your right hand, and put it even on the other hand to your power, then put the plaster and the bandage above, if you have the skill; then strain, and if there is dry bone, do it again, and remove, and cure the wound as long as it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ribs of the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Very rarely does the backbone of the ribs break, and if it does, it is not often due to a slight movement of the neck; and making it long, and declining towards the spine, and coming to the bone, it causes great pain, swelling, and inflammation where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it, as high as the fractured part; and scrape away the broken pieces and the bone shape; and if the fracture is only at the top, then align it until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines towards the inside, then place the limb above its belly, until the restoration of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have placed it evenly, then place the plaster on top, then place a splint of wood or bone, and hold the fractured part so that it does not move; and apply the limb away from the sides, until the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their good side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess occurs, do not touch it until the abscess is calm, and then apply what we have previously mentioned; and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breakage of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the area between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two methods: one method is that you take a piece of bone with a single groove, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two pieces together, and raise them high, and saw through the misaligned part on the seat; then pour some broken bone over the broken arm, until it reaches the ease, and has a nail of bone in the middle, then raise any heavy object or the assistant extends it below; then put the splint together with the pieces, until the broken person returns as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is to place the dislocated joint on its natural place, and hold it with one's hand at its collarbone, then command two ministers that one ties what is above the broken part of their hands, and the others tie from all directions to everything, and extend each to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, hold the ministers away from the broken part and above it, and extend each of them to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the broken part is near the top of the shoulder, then you should place one cord outside the acromion, and the other towards the back, away from the broken part; and similarly, if the broken part is towards the back, then you should place the rope lightly, without labor, until the broken part is even with the top of the shoulder and the back, then make it even, as it should be, and extend it, if necessary, so that it does not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If abscesses arise and come, if you do not restrain them within seven days, and put on them millet flour and rose oil, until the abscesses are calmed; then restrain, and the way of restraining is that you put the plaster on the swollen part, then bring the arm up to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, and restrain on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone does not move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint than the others above the fracture, and have two spaces between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers on each side; then strain against the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less distantly.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the sitting of the splints and the straining, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is healed, let it be tied up for seven days, as we have said; then examine the wound every three days, that it does not become inflamed or infected, or that the discharges do not come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If as directed, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, then only after three days or more, and the pain lies on his back, and his hands are on his stomach; and place the remedy in plain cloth equally, and look every hour of the day or night, that the figure of the member does not move, or that the ligaments are not softened; if as directed by the power of medicine, and give him the food that we have previously placed, in such a way that the food is at the first subtle; and when he begins to recover, it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	It is customary that the shoulder and leg dislocations should be reset in forty days from all; and then one must apply and administer warm baths and remedies of ointments for the limb to recover.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the structure is ugly and deformed, it may take two months or more to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus" and "radius", one of which is small and is that which forms the pocket; and the other is large, and is that which is outside, towards the little finger; perhaps the large humerus alone is broken, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when large bones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it is best to extend them slightly and align them evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then it is best to pull them more strongly; and extend them upwards over the cushion, and stain the pocket of the hand higher than the other fingers, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the tendons cross over themselves, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the tendons suffer no labor; then extend the assistants' arms to the part outside of his hand, or to the elbow, and other assistants above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then place the mirror evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is no piece that can be held by the hand, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the broken one there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the chapter; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses, then glue the cloth of cerate made of red oil and white wax, which is not too hard nor too soft; and bind the cloth subtly, until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cast, and apply the plaster of flour from the mill with abundant oil, then place the splints, and make the splint of the broken bone wider than the others; and it should have six splints or more in various positions: whether the broken bone is in one of the bones, or in two; and it should be held higher than the broken bone than other parts, and always less distant, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are on the broken bone be soft and moist, and not too hard or sharp; and let the thread, by which it is tied, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the joint after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accident occurs to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, it is necessary that you raise the member in hot water, until those itching are soothed; and let the member not be too tightly rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then continue the reduction, and if the joint is broken and the bones are displaced, and similar things, if it addresses.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the tendons cannot come to the member, because it is too tight, it is necessary that you soften it a little, and let it rest for some time, until the tendons are corrected, and then reset.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to harm, let it lie for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Then apply heat to his neck, and let his neck be straight, and avoid movement and stretching, and sleep on his back; and in 30 or 35 days, or perhaps in 20 days, depending on the constitutions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Then apply heat to the back of the hand and avoid it having too many fractures, and it will only hurt once in a while.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the bone of the hand is broken or painful, it is necessary that the pain be crossed and straightened in front of him equally; then put his hand on the extended palm, and extend the ministers to the broken bones, and place them evenly among the fingers, until they are well joined; and apply the plaster and bandages, if there are no abscesses, then place a splint according to the amount of the bone; and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the broken bone is in the paraded part around the belly of the plantar, then make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to wrap it around his broken foot; and then bandage it with a long strip of cloth, and let it be as wide as the palm of the hand, and bandage it as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the broken bone is in the dorsum, then it is necessary to place a splint above, and another below in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and stanch the wound between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fractured bone comes to any of our joints, such as the wrist, if it is out of place, put it back in place, and hold it with the palm, and see if you can lift the fractured bone without moving; and if the fracture is in other joints, such as the index or the others, put it back in place, and bind it with the sound joint that comes after; or you can tie them all together while holding them, which is better, or you can put a splint on top, as you would for a wrist; and take care in the restoration and positioning of abscesses, and attend to what comes next, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken ribs
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the ribcage are often broken, and one can see them when they turn in front and behind; and the restoration is as one lies on the side of the breaker, and the other away from it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the hairs are cut off from his face, then each minister stretches their own line evenly; and this is when the break is brought to the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the ribcage, then one line should be on the side of the breaker, and the other lines away from it.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the glenohumeral joint, and then the ligaments above the glenohumeral joint are stretched, and the extension down; then place the hand on the bone equal to its two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, and if there are no abscesses.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there are abscesses, let it rest and then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap the broken bone twice or three times in a doubled-over bandage and let the excess remain, then bend the leg until the toes reach the root of the foot, and place a long thread between the calf and the leg below the glenohumeral joint, and bring the upper end of the thread above; then bend the broken bone again and place the bandage on top of it, then place a bandage over the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the calf with soft cloth to equalize the tension, then begin to bandage around three or four times above the break; and as you go higher than the break, and lessen the tension; then take two threads that you have placed between the leg and the calf, and three bandages that are above, then return to the top of the thread, until you reach below the knee; and if it does not move from its place, then let it remain, so that there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it is dislocated, if you pull it and direct it as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that you can grasp, then it should be set, if possible; and if not, then you must break the limb and remove the fragments; and the cure is as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never break the neck in such a way that one puts these things on it, as in the dislocation of the arm; nevertheless, in such a restoration made, it does not cause great pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is said that the neck is restored in a few days, or slightly more or less, according to the different constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin path
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	There are few breaks in the groin path, but it often bleeds.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a small cut or puncture, and it has to all wounds, both inside and outside, and it feels very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done by putting together what is torn apart, as much as it can be; then put on the plaster, and if you have skill, place a round bandage, and hold it as it should be, then reward all the preparations that we have said in other breaks, such as abscess and similar; put to each accident what it needs, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" on the right side, and the other is called "foscile"; and they are all as fragile as those in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the work is complete. And if both bones are broken at once, then the leg returns to its normal state from all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then it returns in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then it causes great pain and can be seen clearly; and it returns outwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, apply gentle traction, and make it even, and tie the fractures equally; but anyway, it is necessary to limit the breakage and the deformity, and there are many pieces, that the traction be less and lighter; and mend according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that bind the leg on one side and the other, and be long enough to go from the knee down to the ankle; then wrap them around the leg above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this point the leg will not bend to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one administers the long cloth of the leg, and if it is made properly, and correctly place the leg to prevent movement, and properly do this in the break or where it is wounded; and move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or other accident; if the cure until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of bones due to a fall
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but a bone due to a fall often does not break and has only minor damage, and there is never any serious injury in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bone due to a fall, and you see these bones sticking out above each other, if you put them back on the ground, as if they want to walk, then put your bone where the bones are raised, then press them so much that they return to their place; then apply the ointment and dress with a poultice of two fingers wide, then strap the bone evenly, then wrap cloths around, and other things that you know.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if you release the joint, you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, if you restore them as we have said for the two bones of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the bone, and it should be a little wider, then place the bandage as I have said, and tighten it gradually; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, place a splint according to their quantity, wrapped in a piece of linen, and tighten the bandage from above the splint, so that it does not irritate.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you should not forget the other things I have mentioned about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each accident as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the finger bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of the woman are broken, if the bone is enlarged, then incline it to the back part, and hold it in place; then fill the wound with cotton, and put in as much as possible; then lift the woman, and slowly raise her back, and when the cotton comes out of the wound, the bone returns with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, return it, and do this for seven days or so: then the fracture will be restored, and if you see that it is healing, take a bladder of lamb’s wool, and place it on the bone, and blow all the air out of the bladder; then inflate the bladder again, until the bladder is full inside: nature will restore the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it in place for several days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of the hand is broken, or of the woman, if it is reset as we have said in the bone of the shoulder; and these nearby breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and his use to this book, and pays attention to it.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the broken bone signifies in many positions the right way of restoration: understand this then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the thigh, when it is broken, take a goose's neck and blow the thigh; then wrap it in cloths, and leave it three days or around, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the ribs or shoulder or similar, that they be cleansed immediately, so that the cleansings that we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is cleansed, and the bone is reduced, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the fractured bone in that same hour, or the next day, before infection comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if infection comes, then leave the restoration until the next day, until the infection is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will cause bad accidents to occur.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken tooth appears above the gum, it is necessary that you slightly press it lightly with your fingers, extending it gently.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable to be placed in your hands, then use this iron tool, which is seven or eight spans long, and its width depends on the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the mirror to take three or four, according to how much he has in each case of breaking; and it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not painfully press against the limb at your work, and it should be sharp behind, and thick in the middle in front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the patient's finger should be placed on the top of the bone's apparent head; and the hammer is struck once, as much as it returns, and they are evenly aligned against each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone until the instruments have hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, then use a suitable tool from among the instruments, such as a saw or a chisel, to your power; then roughen and make small scratches on the remaining part of the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the pain is great afterwards, massage that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do this until it is in its natural place, then massage the wound with sterile black wine, and properly if it was in a state of swelling; and do not put anything on the wound except oil, that it does not bring on putrefaction and corruption; then administer these things as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times this has been done by fools, and they have brought on infection or death or corrosion at any time; and let the wounds be more gentle and softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that no evil event has occurred, as we have said, and you relieve pain to the limb, but it does not require a splint; then wrap around, in place of a splint, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is closing, remove whatever you have put on top of the wound, and apply a healing ointment, such as tetra-pharmacon and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to move the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, as long as it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be aligned in such a way that the bow correlates lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue to be out of place, and it cannot be set but remains bowed, cut away the small pieces of bone, because it is necessary that you cover the wound with a tent, and remove all those unnecessary pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the limb, or in another way of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what it says in its previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and open on the limb, like the bones of the knee or of the shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not remove it immediately, because often many die, but leave it until it can heal; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the sudden blows that come to the soothe
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the fractured bone, even when it is near the joint, and the unfortunate thing is to see the shape of the limb; and by chance cannot do the member's natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, if we have fresh fracture: if you administer stiffening medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, aceite, and similar things, in such a way that you grind any of these or all together, and mix with stiffening wine or abundant honey or vinegar; and put it on the broken bone in stoppers, and hold it tightly, and do not let go in hands later; and then remove it, and start another one until the fracture is healed; or you hold a piece of plaster well made; because the property of the plaster is that it removes all swellings above the limbs; and if the fracture has become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, if the cope above, and making the excess apparent; or you reset it at any saw, until it is healed, and care until it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb after a fracture
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and the limb remains weak and thin afterward, this can be due to many causes: one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and could not reach the member; or because of too much swelling; or because of too great movements, not in its place; or because it has little blood in its body, it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you reduce the pain, and make the body tense, until the swelling is not multiplied in it; and give baths, and give joy and ease; then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great swelling, and the swelling often of hot water, until the swelling goes to the member; and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a crooked limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is deformed, but it does not affect its original nature: if you do not believe the people who say that one should break the limb completely new, and many have done this in our land; and these practices are blamed, and great harm comes from them, and perhaps death; however, if the adjustments and twists are fresh, it is necessary to apply hot water or softening herbs cooked, such as willow bark, roots, and marshmallow, and similar things; and make a mollifying plaster, such as good-quality hay, and grind mustard with goose grease or sunflower oil, and apply it on top; or take figs that are greasy, and grind them with linseed, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is it necessary to apply pressure continuously and for a long time to a joint that is already swollen by moisture.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And you should allow movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is awakened and hardened, like a stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, if it covers the joint, make a thin incision; and apply a poultice and rest in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, it must now be brought back against the shoulder blade.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, if the shoulder swells, and perhaps if it is reset to the bone; for it does not matter that it be moved too much where it is swollen: many times, spasms and other pains are brought on; therefore, when this happens, first soothe the pain, then leave it, until the abscess is calmed; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each member as it comes back to its bone.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations of the shoulder joint from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are two ways in which the mandibles can be dislocated: either they are slightly displaced from their place and somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and preventing the tongue from holding the saliva in the mouth, nor can he close his mouth, and wrapping his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns to its place in many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if she is whole and completed, it is necessary that you reset her hastily, and do not delay; and in such a manner that the ministers tie the head of the bad joint, and push the teeth slightly out of the one of her hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand be outside, to hold even; and command the bad joint to soften, its jaws, and move them from all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the teeth become even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially if both jaws are involved, raise the tips of high hot oil and oil, until they are lightly reset; do not delay the resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are returned evenly, and the jaw with the painful joint is well closed to prevent softening, put wet cloths on the face made of rose oil and wax, then lightly bind them with soft bands; let the pains sleep on their back, and their jaws should be between two cushions, so that they do not move to the left or right, nor make any effort to open their mouth, but take light food until the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed; then change what they want lightly, and do not exert themselves to open their mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset to their original position within an hour, and are not converted back to their usual position, then fevers and sweating ensue, along with vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then it is a sign of danger; many times those who have it die within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot be removed from the side of the chest without breaking it, and it is not reset once dislocated, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient should lie on their back, and extend their arms; then press the bone firmly against your palm, and it will return; then apply the ointment and bandage, and hold it in place; the one who is lying on their side cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is dislocated once, then reset it as we have said; then apply the ointment and bandage, and hold it in place, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and thus the same is done for the shoulder spica, when it is healed from its bone.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder dislocates: one is that it dislocates at the part of the armpit to the outside; and the second is at the part of the elbow; and sometimes at the part above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inwards through the nerves; and often it dislocates outwards towards the armpit, especially to those who have little fat, because to these it dislocates harshly; to those who have enough fat, it dislocates gently, and returns gently.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, some men have had compression or crushing, and the shoulder has swollen with an abscess, and thought it was dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must examine him until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is known that the dislocation is when it is below the acromion, and it sets apart the sick shoulder from the healthy one, and you will find between them clear differences; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a fossa, and below the acromion the top of the shoulder, as if it were an os; and the evil cannot move its hand to its neck, nor move from any movements; and also, if it is dislocated above, if it is not hidden, because you will clearly see it at the back; and this kind of dislocation is not other than to be reset, when it is new, or when the evil is in the dislocation.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister lifts the hand of the injured person upwards, then places his fingers below the joint, and pulls the joint upwards to the shoulder; and the minister lifts the hand, and extends it upwards, then puts it down quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if she does not come as we have said in the previous days, then it is necessary that the dislocated joint be soaked in hot water; and the minister should soften and moisten it with a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and apply it; then place the dislocated joint on its back, and put a cloth of equal width, neither too soft nor too hard, under the joint, then put the foot of the injured person on top of the cloth, and lift the shoulder gently, and take the hand of the injured person; and other ministers should wet the head of the injured person, so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder is now back in place, and if you see that it is held in place by following this method: and it is necessary that you have someone who is larger than the injured person; and stand on the side of the chest, and push the shoulder of the injured person away from under the dislocated joint, and lift the joint upwards, so that the dislocated joint hangs in the air; and other ministers should take the hand of the injured person down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the pain is too light, you can do nothing with it, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting is done in another way: and it is that you take a long thin stick made of wood, like a dart, but not too thick or too sharp; then put it outside the painful part, but with a soft cloth on top, and the joint should be extended along the length of the stick; then extend your hand from the other side in the same way, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if for all these things that we have said, she does not want to return, do this cure: take a stick of two arms wide and four fingers long, which has the head round to enter through the opening from outside, in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie the head of the dislocated shoulder with a soft cloth that was not causing the pain, then remove it from the dislocated position; extend the affected arm upwards, and tie the dislocation above the elbow; and place the hand on the shoulder of the other hand, then put the arm over a wide-bladed knife, and extend the hands downwards, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint is now healed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when she is healed in whatever way it may be, you should place a soft cloth pad evenly over the shoulder and around, then apply the plaster with powder from the mill, with incense and a little egg, over the entire shoulder and around, then remove the bandage evenly from the shoulder, and return the limb to the plaster, and embrace the hand to its collar, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he change little, until the limb is comforted, for it will heal faster; then change after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiff and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is strong due to moisture that has come, or for other reasons, then you should administer cautery at three places, as it is placed in front of or in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise the arm above, then cut the nerve at the top of the shoulder that is twisted or stretched or softened; and cut that the joint has never been fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is above the knees and behind, or below, is caused by impact and stretching of the hands, and there is another remedy; and it should be treated until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if afterwards the member becomes stiff and moves slowly, then use the hairs many times in a bath until that stiffness is relieved, and returns to its original form.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	That the joint of the shoulder is dislocated and returns; and it has been dislocated from all parts, and even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not yet healed, for one can see and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	When you join the dislocated shoulder with its joint, then open it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bear the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset the joint as soon as possible, because if it is not reset, it will be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is in the back; it is better than other dislocations, and causes more great pain, and perhaps it kills.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend your hand to your two hands; and its arms are expanded, and the hands of the other on either side of the shoulder, out and in, and bring the joint together with its tendons together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and holds the root of the palm which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to the place, then apply strong extension; and if two people extend the arm, and hold it with two people, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from each part, then having wrapped a long and wide cloth around it; when you see the joint at the hand, if there is any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint together, as much as it returns; and when it is in place, put a dry plaster with some honey on it, and hold it together, and put the arm against the bad side, and leave it for some time, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the limb, and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then restart the bandage and the limb, and leave it thus for some time, until it is firmly placed; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if it feels gripping after the return of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or you put above the joint a piece of fat mutton, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and put in a bath; and when it sweats, rub the joint immediately, then put the piece of fat mutton back on, and then put in a bath; and so do twice or three times until it is healed; and if you see, then put above the joint a piece of moist cloth warmed with butter, and press it on; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is lighter than other joints. Nevertheless, it should be quickly reset to its place in the same moment it is dislocated, as long as the bones are swollen or there is an abscess present.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is done by placing the misaligned hand on a table, extending the fingers of the hand, and aligning the palm so that it rests on the appearance of the joint, and gently pushing until it returns to its place. Then, you should check if it is properly reset; then, place the misaligned hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the patient's hand on a table, and the assistant puts their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is well. If not, apply warm compresses to the abscess and let it rest until you can begin again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some time, the joint will remain twisted; and do not pull anything from the patient until the hand is clean, and cannot be stretched: then cut the nerve or artery; if there is no other method than to stretch by fire through the skin, and perhaps nothing else is better.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put the plaster that we have mentioned above, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no swelling, then apply hot water mixed with salt, and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The two fingers of the hand are not dislocated at each part, neither at the back of the palm nor at the belly; therefore, keep the finger straight and reset the dislocation to your fist as long as it returns, then support the head of the finger, and move it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for three days, and then put it in place that day; and bind it as we have said, and remove it the next day, and make it move, and reattach it; and do this often until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in other parts.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	displacement of the spine on the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine on the back or neck is dislocated, and there are many dislocations, there is no cure, as the patient dies from the pain.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are such that the excretions jump out involuntarily, and cannot be held, and often the limbs become soft, or the two thighs or the two arms or one, and often the spine moves at the back; this is called "gibosity": the cure is to reward the gibosity if it came from childhood: if there is no cure or healing for the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.
