And those that come from falling or from percussions or similar things, they said in the old ways of cures by great words, but I have abbreviated them according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the region that comes to the front of the shoulder, there is no engine or health; and also the one that comes directly to the second rib, and one cannot cure it other than the proper one that comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the hairs should be stretched out over its face evenly, and he should have some strain outside of him, so that he does not bleed; then make the first bandage at the top in earth form, and the other at the bottom, and tie one ligature outside of the hairs of the wound, and the other as the hips, and as the knees, and as the ankles; and two ministers should hold the ligatures, one at the top and the others at the bottom, among the two bandages; and they should be well tied, the bandage as we have said, and the hand puts its palms over the spine evenly, until it is healed.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this treatment, take a long table of three arms' length, and twist it out of shape, and the hairs should be on one side, and bite the edge of the table from the outside, then place the middle of the table on the spine; and put the mirrors on the other end of the table, and press firmly until it returns to its original position; and if you see, do it with the hand that turns back.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should tie two ropes at the top of the shoulder of one arm, and on both sides of the foot, and between each rope, on either side, a palm's length of long rope; and in each rope, one knot, or the twisted part, and let the ropes be firmly on the ground so they do not move; and between each two ropes, one rope turning around, towards the direction the twisted part turns, and a small rope of a palm's length of long rope, to turn the twisted part; and then tie the ligament that is among the tendons to the twisted part towards the shoulder, and the other ligament to the foot on the other twisted part, and each minister should turn their twisted part along the entire limb, and the master should put the spine in place as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with an abundance of honey, and then wrap it, and then place it on a plate of three inches of length, which supports the neck of the spine and the part of the spine, as we have said, and use subtle pressure until they are healed; and if anything comes at the end of health, then administer medicines that are softening and pain-relieving, with the remedy that we have mentioned before; and never give one piece of plaster, and never appear in the back spine of the back, and be careful not to have presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of shoulder dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	There are no fractures of the shoulder joint and the shoulder joint is dislocated in four parts: inwards and outwards, and forwards and backwards; and more inwards than that, and less dislocated forwards and backwards.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of the dislocation inwards is such that when the crooked leg is joined with the straight one, it is longer and more open than the straight one, and cannot double its knee to the fire; and this is because the patient has an abscess underneath.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes after this is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has it in front are that he is well-aligned with his leg according to completion; however, if he doubles over with pain in the groin, and they want to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and retains his urine, and swells with anger, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has it in back are that he cannot spread his groin, nor double over, and the other leg is more twisted than the other, and the anger is softened, and the shoulder is dislocated to the side of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The symptoms of this type of dislocation are such that if the joint is reset, it remains in place according to its natural position, and there is no treatment; and there is no need for presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, you must return the joint, extend it, and move it to the left and right; perhaps if it returns, and there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must apply one strong minister, and extend the leg strongly at two fingers, or at one finger that is tied above the knee; and other ministers hold their hand over the tailbone in a certain way so that they bite their hands off their sides, then pinch the skin on the back; and some tie the head of the limb; and extend up and down all at once, until the pain is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must treat its similarity. When the dislocation is in the pelvis, you should support the misaligned limb on its healthy side, then place the bandage under the root of the thigh, and the limb that is outside the groin, then extend the bandage upwards towards the groin and the hip; then take other ministers to hold the large thigh muscle misaligned, and stretch it properly: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is less painful than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary to tie the two hairs of the limp together with a strong rope above the two heels, and above the two ankles, and let the limp leg be stretched out two fingers more than the others; then it should be suspended over the top of a stick, and let the other arm hang down two arms' length from the ground; then command the minister to grasp the base of the neck, and let another minister hold the limp, who should grasp the neck formally, for the joint is now approaching.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in the lower part, then massage the hairs, as we have said in the one with gout, and pull the rope properly over the limp leg and also at the foot; then put two ties, one at the head and the other at the foot, then fold the tie between the legs of the limp in the proper form; and place moist cloths around it, so that it does not become dry, then extend each minister towards him, and the patient puts the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on the table, and press it as we have described in the gibbosity, and grind the bones on the flat side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the misaligned leg firmly, as I have said; and place the fingers of the pain above the crooked leg, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not necessary to extend the misaligned leg downwards, nor to lift it up, but it should be as it was when the hips were dislocated in the back, as we have said about lying on the two hips; and it should be on its face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint at the table; and it will be good when the legs are extended, and they are even; then bend the knees, and put the poultice, and the strap of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three days or four, then release it, and put the poultice on; and if you see that they are even, remove the strap, as before, and leave it for three days; then release it, and make the limb move well, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: namely, from within and without, and from behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg at the hip, and if they cannot bend it at the hip, it indicates that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if possible, and place your back against their face, and place their foot on yours; then take their shoulder to your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the shoulder correctly; and another minister extends their foot, until the shoulder returns to its place, and the sign is that they can bend their leg at the hip lightly; and apply the plaster to it, and support the leg against the hip for a few minutes or hours, then release it; and do not work on the patient any more until their members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	If the limbs are not broken, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the back, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The feet are never bruised and never completely dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the bone is out of place, and feels tender to the touch at the part where it is dislocated: the reflexes are light, and one should gently extend them slightly when they are pressed alone.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated completely, you should straighten the painful part correctly, and hold it with your hands above the ankle; then grasp the bone with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and strongly tap the bone upwards; do this twice, as we have said, bending and drawing the bone; if it returns, it is well; if not, if you repeat the procedure, it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, place the painful part on its back on the ground, and firmly press between his thighs, and wrap cloths around, so that it does not bend the bone; then hold the hands on his thigh, and another person extends the bone to his hands or to the ligament, so that they hold it above the bone; then extend all the hands equally, and the cloths should be placed between the thighs of the painful part to retain the dislocation while you are extending it; then place the bones evenly in your hands, and another person holds the leg straight at the back, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it does not heal, put the plaster on and apply pressure above, and let the swelling form, and tie the leg to the foot, and support the tendons that are above the ankle behind, so that the joints are not too stretched; then leave it for two or three days, and if the swelling does not subside, then let it rest for another two or three days, and after that, let it go to walk for four days; and if it goes before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is necessary to treat it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	For the fire cautery, instruct
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they need to be stretched, it is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no way out of place, then you should sit the patient on a chair or table straight up, and put your hand on what opens these joints, then press firmly with your hand until it returns; and when it is even, and there is nothing open, then remove the sole of the foot from the table, put a table to the two knees, then stretch it firmly, and leave it for three hours, then release; and let him rest, until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, and do not know the art well, and have not used it long, and are not pitiful and merciful and late; and at the beginning of things, use gentle remedies for abscesses, and leave the wound in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the member now, as long as the abscesses are coming; and when the member is in place, administer gentle remedies for abscesses, and cure the wound, as it should be, by frequent drying; and if with dislocation there is a breakage, and small bones are to be removed, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard against entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, because it is better for you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your armor and body.
Amen	For the fire cautery
